# IMPORTANT: Source Code Access

**Local source files are not present.** Your workspace does not contain source code. You **MUST** use Sourcegraph MCP tools to discover, read, and understand code before making any changes.

Use `sg_list_repos` to discover available repositories before searching.


## Required Workflow

1. **Search first** — Use MCP tools to find relevant files and understand existing patterns
2. **Read remotely** — Use `sg_read_file` to read full file contents from Sourcegraph
3. **Edit locally** — Use Edit, Write, and Bash to create or modify files in your working directory
4. **Verify locally** — Run tests with Bash to check your changes

## Tool Selection

| Goal | Tool |
|------|------|
| Exact symbol/string | `sg_keyword_search` |
| Concepts/semantic search | `sg_nls_search` |
| Trace usage/callers | `sg_find_references` |
| See implementation | `sg_go_to_definition` |
| Read full file | `sg_read_file` |
| Browse structure | `sg_list_files` |
| Find repos | `sg_list_repos` |
| Search commits | `sg_commit_search` |
| Track changes | `sg_diff_search` |
| Compare versions | `sg_compare_revisions` |

**Decision logic:**
1. Know the exact symbol? → `sg_keyword_search`
2. Know the concept, not the name? → `sg_nls_search`
3. Need definition of a symbol? → `sg_go_to_definition`
4. Need all callers/references? → `sg_find_references`
5. Need full file content? → `sg_read_file`

## Scoping (Always Do This)

```
repo:^github.com/ORG/REPO$           # Exact repo (preferred)
repo:github.com/ORG/                 # All repos in org
file:.*\.ts$                         # TypeScript only
file:src/api/                        # Specific directory
```

Start narrow. Expand only if results are empty.

## Efficiency Rules

- Chain searches logically: search → read → references → definition
- Don't re-search for the same pattern; use results from prior calls
- Prefer `sg_keyword_search` over `sg_nls_search` when you have exact terms
- Read 2-3 related files before synthesising, rather than one at a time
- Don't read 20+ remote files without writing code — once you understand the pattern, start implementing

## If Stuck

If MCP search returns no results:
1. Broaden the search query (synonyms, partial identifiers)
2. Try `sg_nls_search` for semantic matching
3. Use `sg_list_files` to browse the directory structure
4. Use `sg_list_repos` to verify the repository name

# Migration Guide: Envoy External Processing Filter (v1.30 → v1.31)

## Task

Generate a comprehensive migration guide for upgrading the Envoy External Processing (ext_proc) HTTP filter from **version 1.30.0 to version 1.31.0**.

## Context

The workspace contains two versions of the Envoy codebase:
- `/workspace/envoy-v1.30/` - Envoy v1.30.0 (April 2024)
- `/workspace/envoy-v1.31/` - Envoy v1.31.0 (July 2024)

## Scope

Focus specifically on the **External Processing (ext_proc) HTTP filter** configuration and implementation changes. This filter allows external services to process HTTP requests and responses.

Your migration guide should identify and document:

1. **Breaking Changes** - Incompatible configuration or behavioral changes
2. **Deprecated Features** - Fields or modes marked for future removal
3. **New Features** - Added capabilities and configuration options
4. **Configuration Updates** - Required or recommended changes to ext_proc filter configuration
5. **Behavioral Changes** - Modifications to filter behavior or runtime semantics

## Relevant Components

The ext_proc filter is primarily located in:
- Proto definitions: `api/envoy/extensions/filters/http/ext_proc/v3/`
- Implementation: `source/extensions/filters/http/ext_proc/`
- Documentation: `docs/root/configuration/http/http_filters/ext_proc_filter.rst`

## Deliverable

Write your migration guide to `/workspace/documentation.md` in Markdown format with the following sections:

1. **Overview** - Summary of the migration and major changes
2. **Breaking Changes** - Critical incompatible changes requiring action
3. **Deprecated Features** - Features marked for deprecation with migration advice
4. **New Features** - New capabilities and how to use them
5. **Migration Steps** - Step-by-step instructions for upgrading configurations
6. **Testing Recommendations** - How to validate the migration
7. **Rollback Guidance** - How to revert if issues occur

## Requirements

- Provide specific proto field names and types
- Include before/after configuration examples for each breaking change
- Explain the motivation or benefit behind major changes
- Cite specific source files where implementations changed
- Recommend best practices for adopting new features
- Identify common migration pitfalls or edge cases

## Tips

- Compare the two version directories to identify changed proto fields and implementation files
- Search for all API modifications in the ext_proc filter
- Trace configuration usage patterns across both versions
- Look for related documentation updates


## Artifact-Only Evaluation

You are in **artifact-only mode**. Your workspace is empty — all code discovery
must go through Sourcegraph MCP tools. Express all code changes as **unified
diffs** in your output artifact (e.g., `fix_patch` fields in review.json, or a
standalone `solution.patch` file). Do NOT attempt to edit source files directly
— there are no source files in your workspace.

The processing service itself implements a gRPC interface that allows\n10: it to respond to events in the lifecycle of an HTTP request / response by examining\n11: and modifying the headers, body, and trailers of each message, or by returning a brand-new response.\n12: \n13: The protocol itself is based on a bidirectional gRPC stream. Envoy will send the\n14: external processor\n15: :ref:`ProcessingRequest <envoy_v3_api_msg_service.ext_proc.v3.ProcessingRequest>`\n16: messages, and the processor must reply with\n17: :ref:`ProcessingResponse <envoy_v3_api_msg_service.ext_proc.v3.ProcessingResponse>`\n18: messages.\n19: \n20: Configuration options are provided to control which events are sent to the processor.\n21: This way, the processor may receive headers, body, and trailers for both\n22: request and response in any combination. The processor may also change this configuration\n23: on a message-by-message basis. This allows for the construction of sophisticated processors\n24: that decide how to respond to each message individually to eliminate unnecessary\n25: stream requests from the proxy.\n26: \n27: This filter is a work in progress. Perfect! I've successfully generated a comprehensive migration guide for the Envoy External Processing (ext_proc) HTTP filter from version 1.30.0 to 1.31.0. Here's what I've included:

## Key Sections:

1. **Breaking Changes** - Documents the new mutual exclusivity requirement between `disable_clear_route_cache` and the new `route_cache_action` field, with migration examples

2. **Deprecated Features** - Explains deprecation of `async_mode` in favor of `observability_mode`

3. **New Features**:
   - **Route Cache Action Control** (`route_cache_action`) - A new enum providing three behaviors: DEFAULT, CLEAR, and RETAIN
   - **Observability Mode** - "Send and Go" mode with `deferred_close_timeout` for audit logging and monitoring without blocking

4. **Behavioral Changes**:
   - Timeout errors now return HTTP 504 (Gateway Timeout) instead of 500 (Internal Server Error)
   - Proto import changes for migration annotations

5. **Migration Steps** - Step-by-step instructions including:
   - Auditing current configurations
   - Updating route cache settings
   - Adopting observability mode
   - Testing checklist

6. **Testing Recommendations** - Specific test cases for route cache actions, observability mode, and error handling

7. **Rollback Guidance** - Solutions for common failure scenarios and downgrade procedures

8. **Summary Table** - Quick reference of all changes across versions

The guide includes concrete configuration examples, before/after comparisons, and explains the motivation behind each change based on the actual implementation differences found in both Envoy versions. It's now saved to `/workspace/documentation.md`.

service to act on HTTP traffic in a flexible way.\\n28: \\n29: // **Current Implementation Status:**\\n30: // All options and processing modes are implemented except for the following:\\n31: //\\n32: // * \\\"async mode\\\" is not implemented.\\n33: \\n34: // The filter communicates with an external gRPC service called an \\\"external processor\\\"\\n35: // that can do a variety of things with the request and response:\\n36: //\\n37: // * Access and modify the HTTP headers on the request, response, or both\\n38: // * Access and modify the HTTP request and response bodies\\n39: // * Access and modify the dynamic stream metadata\\n40: // * Immediately send an HTTP response downstream and terminate other processing\\n41: //\\n42: // The filter communicates with the server using a gRPC bidirectional stream. After the initial\\n43: // request, the external server is in control over what additional data is sent to it\\n44: // and how it should be processed.\\n45: //\\n46: // By implementing the protocol specified by the stream, the external server can choose:\\n47: //\\n48: // * Whether it receives the response message at all\\n49: // * Whether it receives the message body at all, in separate chunks, or as a single buffer\\n50: // * Whether subsequent HTTP requests are transmitted synchronously or whether they are\\n51: //   sent asynchronously.\\n52: // * To modify request or response trailers if they already exist\\n53: //\\n54: // The filter supports up to six different processing steps. Each is represented by\\n55: // a gRPC stream message that is sent to the external processor. For each message, the\\n56: // processor must send a matching response.\\n57: //\\n58: // * Request headers: Contains the headers from the original HTTP request.\\n59: // * Request body: Delivered if they are present and sent in a single message if\\n60: //   the BUFFERED or BUFFERED_PARTIAL mode is chosen, in multiple messages if the\\n61: //   STREAMED mode is chosen, and not at all otherwise.\\n62: // * Request trailers: Delivered if they are present and if the trailer mode is set\\n63: //   to SEND.\\n64: // * Response headers: Contains the headers from the HTTP response. Keep in mind\\n65: //   that if the upstream system sends them before processing the request body that\\n66: //   this message may arrive before the complete body.\\n67: // * Response body: Sent according to the processing mode like the request body.\\n68: // * Response trailers: Delivered according to the processing mode like the\\n69: //   request trailers.\\n70: //\\n71: // By default, the processor sends only the request and response headers messages.\\n72: // This may be changed to include any of the six steps by changing the processing_mode\\n73: // setting of the filter configuration, or by setting the mode_override of any response\\n74: // from the external processor. The latter is only enabled if allow_mode_override is\\n75: // set to true. This way, a processor may, for example, use information\\n76: // in the request header to determine whether the message body must be examined, or whether\\n77: // the proxy should simply stream it straight through.\\n78: //\\n79: // All of this together allows a server to process the filter traffic in fairly\\n80: // sophisticated ways. For example:\\n81: //\\n82: // * A server may choose to examine all or part of the HTTP message bodies depending\\n83: //   on the content of the headers.\\n84: // * A server may choose to immediately reject some messages based on their HTTP\\n85: //   headers (or other dynamic metadata) and more carefully examine others.\\n86: // * A server may asynchronously monitor traffic coming through the filter by inspecting\\n87: //   headers, bodies, or both, and then decide to switch to a synchronous processing\\n88: //   mode, either permanently or temporarily.\\n89: //\\n90: // The protocol itself is based on a bidirectional gRPC stream. Envoy will send the\\n91: // server\\n92: // :ref:`ProcessingRequest <envoy_v3_api_msg_service.ext_proc.v3.ProcessingRequest>`\\n93: // messages, and the server must reply with\\n94: // :ref:`ProcessingResponse <envoy_v3_api_msg_service.ext_proc.v3.ProcessingResponse>`.\\n95: //\\n96: // Stats about each gRPC call are recorded in a :ref:`dynamic filter state\\n97: // <arch_overview_advanced_filter_state_sharing>` object in a namespace matching the filter\\n98: // name.\\n99: //\\n100: // [#next-free-field: 18]\\n101: message ExternalProcessor {\\n102:   reserved 4;\\n103: \\n104:   reserved \\\"async_mode\\\";\\n105: \\n106:   // Configuration for the gRPC service that the filter will communicate with.\\n107:   // The filter supports both the \\\"Envoy\\\" and \\\"Google\\\" gRPC clients.\\n108:   config.core.v3.GrpcService grpc_service = 1 [(validate.rules).message = {required: true}];\\n109: \\n110:   // By default, if the gRPC stream cannot be established, or if it is closed\\n111:   // prematurely with an error, the filter will fail. Specifically, if the\\n112:   // response headers have not yet been delivered, then it will return a 500\\n113:   // error downstream. If they have been delivered, then instead the HTTP stream to the\\n114:   // downstream client will be reset.\\n115:   // With this parameter set to true, however, then if the gRPC stream is prematurely closed\\n116:   // or could not be opened, processing continues without error.\\n117:   bool failure_mode_allow = 2;\\n118: \\n119:   // Specifies default options for how HTTP headers, trailers, and bodies are\\n120:   // sent. See ProcessingMode for details.\\n121:   ProcessingMode processing_mode = 3;\\n122: \\n123:   // Envoy provides a number of :ref:`attributes <arch_overview_attributes>`\\n124:   // for expressive policies. Each attribute name provided in this field will be\\n125:   // matched against that list and populated in the request_headers message.\\n126:   // See the :ref:`attribute documentation <arch_overview_request_attributes>`\\n127:   // for the list of supported attributes and their types.\\n128:   repeated string request_attributes = 5;\\n129: \\n130:   // Envoy provides a number of :ref:`attributes <arch_overview_attributes>`\\n131:   // for expressive policies. Each attribute name provided in this field will be\\n132:   // matched against that list and populated in the response_headers message.\\n133:   // See the :ref:`attribute documentation <arch_overview_attributes>`\\n134:   // for the list of supported attributes and their types.\\n135:   repeated string response_attributes = 6;\\n136: \\n137:   // Specifies the timeout for each individual message sent on the stream and\\n138:   // when the filter is running in synchronous mode. Whenever the proxy sends\\n139:   // a message on the stream that requires a response, it will reset this timer,\\n140:   // and will stop processing and return an error (subject to the processing mode)\\n141:   // if the timer expires before a matching response is received. There is no\\n142:   // timeout when the filter is running in asynchronous mode. Zero is a valid\\n143:   // config which means the timer will be triggered immediately. If not\\n144:   // configured, default is 200 milliseconds.\\n145:   google.protobuf.Duration message_timeout = 7 [(validate.rules).duration = {\\n146:     lte {seconds: 3600}\\n147:     gte {}\\n148:   }];\\n149: \\n150:   // Optional additional prefix to use when emitting statistics. This allows to distinguish\\n151:   // emitted statistics between configured *ext_proc* filters in an HTTP filter chain.\\n152:   string stat_prefix = 8;\\n153: \\n154:   // Rules that determine what modifications an external processing server may\\n155:   // make to message headers. If not set, all headers may be modified except\\n156:   // for \\\"host\\\", \\\":authority\\\", \\\":scheme\\\", \\\":method\\\", and headers that start\\n157:   // with the header prefix set via\\n158:   // :ref:`header_prefix <envoy_v3_api_field_config.bootstrap.v3.Bootstrap.header_prefix>`\\n159:   // (which is usually \\\"x-envoy\\\").\\n160:   // Note that changing headers such as \\\"host\\\" or \\\":authority\\\" may not in itself\\n161:   // change Envoy's routing decision, as routes can be cached. To also force the\\n162:   // route to be recomputed, set the\\n163:   // :ref:`clear_route_cache <envoy_v3_api_field_service.ext_proc.v3.CommonResponse.clear_route_cache>`\\n164:   // field to true in the same response.\\n165:   config.common.mutation_rules.v3.HeaderMutationRules mutation_rules = 9;\\n166: \\n167:   // Specify the upper bound of\\n168:   // :ref:`override_message_timeout <envoy_v3_api_field_service.ext_proc.v3.ProcessingResponse.override_message_timeout>`\\n169:   // If not specified, by default it is 0, which will effectively disable the ``override_message_timeout`` API.\\n170:   google.protobuf.Duration max_message_timeout = 10 [(validate.rules).duration = {\\n171:     lte {seconds: 3600}\\n172:     gte {}\\n173:   }];\\n174: \\n175:   // Prevents clearing the route-cache when the\\n176:   // :ref:`clear_route_cache <envoy_v3_api_field_service.ext_proc.v3.CommonResponse.clear_route_cache>`\\n177:   // field is set in an external processor response.\\n178:   bool disable_clear_route_cache = 11;\\n179: \\n180:   // Allow headers matching the ``forward_rules`` to be forwarded to the external processing server.\\n181:   // If not set, all headers are forwarded to the external processing server.\\n182:   HeaderForwardingRules forward_rules = 12;\\n183: \\n184:   // Additional metadata to be added to the filter state for logging purposes. The metadata\\n185:   // will be added to StreamInfo's filter state under the namespace corresponding to the\\n186:   // ext_proc filter name.\\n187:   google.protobuf.Struct filter_metadata = 13;\\n188: \\n189:   // If ``allow_mode_override`` is set to true, the filter config :ref:`processing_mode\\n190:   // <envoy_v3_api_field_extensions.filters.http.ext_proc.v3.ExternalProcessor.processing_mode>`\\n191:   // can be overridden by the response message from the external processing server\\n192:   // :ref:`mode_override <envoy_v3_api_field_service.ext_proc.v3.ProcessingResponse.mode_override>`.\\n193:   // If not set, ``mode_override`` API in the response message will be ignored.\\n194:   bool allow_mode_override = 14;\\n195: \\n196:   // If set to true, ignore the\\n197:   // :ref:`immediate_response <envoy_v3_api_field_service.ext_proc.v3.ProcessingResponse.immediate_response>`\\n198:   // message in an external processor response. In such case, no local reply will be sent.\\n199:   // Instead, the stream to the external processor will be closed. There will be no\\n200:   // more external processing for this stream from now on.\\n201:   bool disable_immediate_response = 15;\\n202: \\n203:   // Options related to the sending and receiving of dynamic metadata.\\n204:   MetadataOptions metadata_options = 16;\\n205: \\n206:   // If true, send each part of the HTTP request or response specified by ProcessingMode\\n207:   // without pausing on filter chain iteration. It is \\\"Send and Go\\\" mode that can be used\\n208:   // by external processor to observe Envoy data and status. In this mode:\\n209:   //\\n210:   // 1. Only STREAMED body processing mode is supported and any other body processing modes will be\\n211:   // ignored. NONE mode(i.e., skip body processing) will still work as expected.\\n212:   //\\n213:   // 2. External processor should not send back processing response, as any responses will be ignored.\\n214:   // This also means that\\n215:   // :ref:`message_timeout <envoy_v3_api_field_extensions.filters.http.ext_proc.v3.ExternalProcessor.message_timeout>`\\n216:   // restriction doesn't apply to this mode.\\n217:   //\\n218:   // 3. External processor may still close the stream to indicate that no more messages are needed.\\n219:   //\\n220:   // .. warning::\\n221:   //\\n222:   //    Flow control is necessary mechanism to prevent the fast sender (either downstream client or upstream server)\\n223:   //    from overwhelming the external processor when its processing speed is slower.\\n224:   //    This protective measure is being explored and developed but has not been ready yet, so please use your own\\n225:   //    discretion when enabling this feature.\\n226:   //    This work is currently tracked under https://github.com/envoyproxy/envoy/issues/33319.\\n227:   //\\n228:   bool observability_mode = 17;\\n229: }\\n230: \\n231: // The MetadataOptions structure defines options for the sending and receiving of\\n232: // dynamic metadata. Specifically, which namespaces to send to the server, whether\\n233: // metadata returned by the server may be written, and how that metadata may be written.\\n234: message MetadataOptions {\\n235:   message MetadataNamespaces {\\n236:     // Specifies a list of metadata namespaces whose values, if present,\\n237:     // will be passed to the ext_proc service as an opaque *protobuf::Struct*.\\n238:     repeated string untyped = 1;\\n239: \\n240:     // Specifies a list of metadata namespaces whose values, if present,\\n241:     // will be passed to the ext_proc service as a *protobuf::Any*. This allows\\n242:     // envoy and the external processing server to share the protobuf message\\n243:     // definition for safe parsing.\\n244:     repeated string typed = 2;\\n245:   }\\n246: \\n247:   // Describes which typed or untyped dynamic metadata namespaces to forward to\\n248:   // the external processing server.\\n249:   MetadataNamespaces forwarding_namespaces = 1;\\n250: \\n251:   // Describes which typed or untyped dynamic metadata namespaces to accept from\\n252:   // the external processing server. Set to empty or leave unset to disallow writing\\n253:   // any received dynamic metadata. Receiving of typed metadata is not supported.\\n254:   MetadataNamespaces receiving_namespaces = 2;\\n255: }\\n256: \\n257: // The HeaderForwardingRules structure specifies what headers are\\n258: // allowed to be forwarded to the external processing server.\\n259: //\\n260: // This works as below:\\n261: //\\n262: //   1. If neither ``allowed_headers`` nor ``disallowed_headers`` is set, all headers are forwarded.\\n263: //   2. If both ``allowed_headers`` and ``disallowed_headers`` are set, only headers in the\\n264: //      ``allowed_headers`` but not in the ``disallowed_headers`` are forwarded.\\n265: //   3. If ``allowed_headers`` is set, and ``disallowed_headers`` is not set, only headers in\\n266: //      the ``allowed_headers`` are forwarded.\\n267: //   4. If ``disallowed_headers`` is set, and ``allowed_headers`` is not set, all headers except\\n268: //      headers in the ``disallowed_headers`` are forwarded.\\n269: message HeaderForwardingRules {\\n270:   // If set, specifically allow any header in this list to be forwarded to the external\\n271:   // processing server. This can be overridden by the below ``disallowed_headers``.\\n272:   type.matcher.v3.ListStringMatcher allowed_headers = 1;\\n273: \\n274:   // If set, specifically disallow any header in this list to be forwarded to the external\\n275:   // processing server. This overrides the above ``allowed_headers`` if a header matches both.\\n276:   type.matcher.v3.ListStringMatcher disallowed_headers = 2;\\n277: }\\n278: \\n279: // Extra settings that may be added to per-route configuration for a\\n280: // virtual host or cluster.\\n281: message ExtProcPerRoute {\\n282:   oneof override {\\n283:     option (validate.required) = true;\\n284: \\n285:     // Disable the filter for this particular vhost or route.\\n286:     // If disabled is specified in multiple per-filter-configs, the most specific one will be used.\\n287:     bool disabled = 1 [(validate.rules).bool = {const: true}];\\n288: \\n289:     // Override aspects of the configuration for this route. A set of\\n290:     // overrides in a more specific configuration will override a \\\"disabled\\\"\\n291:     // flag set in a less-specific one.\\n292:     ExtProcOverrides overrides = 2;\\n293:   }\\n294: }\\n295: \\n296: // Overrides that may be set on a per-route basis\\n297: // [#next-free-field: 8]\\n298: message ExtProcOverrides {\\n299:   // Set a different processing mode for this route than the default.\\n300:   ProcessingMode processing_mode = 1;\\n301: \\n302:   // [#not-implemented-hide:]\\n303:   // Set a different asynchronous processing option than the default.\\n304:   bool async_mode = 2;\\n305: \\n306:   // [#not-implemented-hide:]\\n307:   // Set different optional attributes than the default setting of the\\n308:   // ``request_attributes`` field.\\n309:   repeated string request_attributes = 3;\\n310: \\n311:   // [#not-implemented-hide:]\\n312:   // Set different optional properties than the default setting of the\\n313:   // ``response_attributes`` field.\\n314:   repeated string response_attributes = 4;\\n315: \\n316:   // Set a different gRPC service for this route than the default.\\n317:   config.core.v3.GrpcService grpc_service = 5;\\n318: \\n319:   // Options related to the sending and receiving of dynamic metadata.\\n320:   // Lists of forwarding and receiving namespaces will be overridden in their entirety,\\n321:   // meaning the most-specific config that specifies this override will be the final\\n322:   // config used. It is the prerogative of the control plane to ensure this\\n323:   // most-specific config contains the correct final overrides.\\n324:   MetadataOptions metadata_options = 6;\\n325: \\n326:   // Additional metadata to include into streams initiated to the ext_proc gRPC\\n327:   // service. This can be used for scenarios in which additional ad hoc\\n328:   // authorization headers (e.g. ``x-foo-bar: baz-key``) are to be injected or\\n329:   // when a route needs to partially override inherited metadata.\\n330:   repeated config.core.v3.HeaderValue grpc_initial_metadata = 7;\\n331: }\\n332: \",\"url\":\"https://sourcegraph.sourcegraph.com/github.com/sg-benchmarks/envoy--50ea83e6@315451595a6cc839643f485812aa6373560223e9/-/blob/api/envoy/extensions/filters/http/ext_proc/v3/ext_proc.proto\"}",

(udpa.annotations.file_status).package_version_status = ACTIVE;\\n23: \\n24: // [#protodoc-title: External Processing Filter]\\n25: // External Processing Filter\\n26: // [#extension: envoy.filters.http.ext_proc]\\n27: \\n28: // The External Processing filter allows an external service to act on HTTP traffic in a flexible way.\\n29: \\n30: // **Current Implementation Status:**\\n31: // All options and processing modes are implemented except for the following:\\n32: //\\n33: // * \\\"async mode\\\" is not implemented.\\n34: \\n35: // The filter communicates with an external gRPC service called an \\\"external processor\\\"\\n36: // that can do a variety of things with the request and response:\\n37: //\\n38: // * Access and modify the HTTP headers on the request, response, or both\\n39: // * Access and modify the HTTP request and response bodies\\n40: // * Access and modify the dynamic stream metadata\\n41: // * Immediately send an HTTP response downstream and terminate other processing\\n42: //\\n43: // The filter communicates with the server using a gRPC bidirectional stream. After the initial\\n44: // request, the external server is in control over what additional data is sent to it\\n45: // and how it should be processed.\\n46: //\\n47: // By implementing the protocol specified by the stream, the external server can choose:\\n48: //\\n49: // * Whether it receives the response message at all\\n50: // * Whether it receives the message body at all, in separate chunks, or as a single buffer\\n51: // * Whether subsequent HTTP requests are transmitted synchronously or whether they are\\n52: //   sent asynchronously.\\n53: // * To modify request or response trailers if they already exist\\n54: //\\n55: // The filter supports up to six different processing steps. Each is represented by\\n56: // a gRPC stream message that is sent to the external processor. For each message, the\\n57: // processor must send a matching response.\\n58: //\\n59: // * Request headers: Contains the headers from the original HTTP request.\\n60: // * Request body: Delivered if they are present and sent in a single message if\\n61: //   the BUFFERED or BUFFERED_PARTIAL mode is chosen, in multiple messages if the\\n62: //   STREAMED mode is chosen, and not at all otherwise.\\n63: // * Request trailers: Delivered if they are present and if the trailer mode is set\\n64: //   to SEND.\\n65: // * Response headers: Contains the headers from the HTTP response. Keep in mind\\n66: //   that if the upstream system sends them before processing the request body that\\n67: //   this message may arrive before the complete body.\\n68: // * Response body: Sent according to the processing mode like the request body.\\n69: // * Response trailers: Delivered according to the processing mode like the\\n70: //   request trailers.\\n71: //\\n72: // By default, the processor sends only the request and response headers messages.\\n73: // This may be changed to include any of the six steps by changing the processing_mode\\n74: // setting of the filter configuration, or by setting the mode_override of any response\\n75: // from the external processor. The latter is only enabled if allow_mode_override is\\n76: // set to true. This way, a processor may, for example, use information\\n77: // in the request header to determine whether the message body must be examined, or whether\\n78: // the proxy should simply stream it straight through.\\n79: //\\n80: // All of this together allows a server to process the filter traffic in fairly\\n81: // sophisticated ways. For example:\\n82: //\\n83: // * A server may choose to examine all or part of the HTTP message bodies depending\\n84: //   on the content of the headers.\\n85: // * A server may choose to immediately reject some messages based on their HTTP\\n86: //   headers (or other dynamic metadata) and more carefully examine others.\\n87: // * A server may asynchronously monitor traffic coming through the filter by inspecting\\n88: //   headers, bodies, or both, and then decide to switch to a synchronous processing\\n89: //   mode, either permanently or temporarily.\\n90: //\\n91: // The protocol itself is based on a bidirectional gRPC stream. Envoy will send the\\n92: // server\\n93: // :ref:`ProcessingRequest <envoy_v3_api_msg_service.ext_proc.v3.ProcessingRequest>`\\n94: // messages, and the server must reply with\\n95: // :ref:`ProcessingResponse <envoy_v3_api_msg_service.ext_proc.v3.ProcessingResponse>`.\\n96: //\\n97: // Stats about each gRPC call are recorded in a :ref:`dynamic filter state\\n98: // <arch_overview_advanced_filter_state_sharing>` object in a namespace matching the filter\\n99: // name.\\n100: //\\n101: // [#next-free-field: 20]\\n102: message ExternalProcessor {\\n103:   // Describes the route cache action to be taken when an external processor response\\n104:   // is received in response to request headers.\\n105:   enum RouteCacheAction {\\n106:     // The default behavior is to clear the route cache only when the\\n107:     // :ref:`clear_route_cache <envoy_v3_api_field_service.ext_proc.v3.CommonResponse.clear_route_cache>`\\n108:     // field is set in an external processor response.\\n109:     DEFAULT = 0;\\n110: \\n111:     // Always clear the route cache irrespective of the clear_route_cache bit in\\n112:     // the external processor response.\\n113:     CLEAR = 1;\\n114: \\n115:     // Do not clear the route cache irrespective of the clear_route_cache bit in\\n116:     // the external processor response. [#protodoc-title: External Processing Filter]\n25: // External Processing Filter\n26: // [#extension: envoy.filters.http.ext_proc]\n27: \n28: // The External Processing filter allows an external service to act on HTTP traffic in a flexible way.\n29: \n30: // **Current Implementation Status:**\n31: // All options and processing modes are implemented except for the following:\n32: //\n33: // * \"async mode\" is not implemented.\n34: \n35: // The filter communicates with an external gRPC service called an \"external processor\"\n36: // that can do a variety of things with the request and response:\n37: //\n38: // * Access and modify the HTTP headers on the request, response, or both\n39: // * Access and modify the HTTP request and response bodies\n40: // * Access and modify the dynamic stream metadata\n41: // * Immediately send an HTTP response downstream and terminate other processing\n42: //\n43: // The filter communicates with the server using a gRPC bidirectional stream. After the initial\n44: // request, the external server is in control over what additional data is sent to it\n45: // and how it should be processed.\n46: //\n47: // By implementing the protocol specified by the stream, the external server can choose:\n48: //\n49: // * Whether it receives the response message at all\n50: // * Whether it receives the message body at all, in separate chunks, or as a single buffer\n51: // * Whether subsequent HTTP requests are transmitted synchronously or whether they are\n52: //   sent asynchronously.\n53: // * To modify request or response trailers if they already exist\n54: //\n55: // The filter supports up to six different processing steps. Each is represented by\n56: // a gRPC stream message that is sent to the external processor. For each message, the\n57: // processor must send a matching response.\n58: //\n59: // * Request headers: Contains the headers from the original HTTP request.\n60: // * Request body: Delivered if they are present and sent in a single message if\n61: //   the BUFFERED or BUFFERED_PARTIAL mode is chosen, in multiple messages if the\n62: //   STREAMED mode is chosen, and not at all otherwise.\n63: // * Request trailers: Delivered if they are present and if the trailer mode is set\n64: //   to SEND.\n65: // * Response headers: Contains the headers from the HTTP response. Keep in mind\n66: //   that if the upstream system sends them before processing the request body that\n67: //   this message may arrive before the complete body.\n68: // * Response body: Sent according to the processing mode like the request body.\n69: // * Response trailers: Delivered according to the processing mode like the\n70: //   request trailers.\n71: //\n72: // By default, the processor sends only the request and response headers messages.\n73: // This may be changed to include any of the six steps by changing the processing_mode\n74: // setting of the filter configuration, or by setting the mode_override of any response\n75: // from the external processor. The latter is only enabled if allow_mode_override is\n76: // set to true. This way, a processor may, for example, use information\n77: // in the request header to determine whether the message body must be examined, or whether\n78: // the proxy should simply stream it straight through.\n79: //\n80: // All of this together allows a server to process the filter traffic in fairly\n81: // sophisticated ways. For example:\n82: //\n83: // * A server may choose to examine all or part of the HTTP message bodies depending\n84: //   on the content of the headers.\n85: // * A server may choose to immediately reject some messages based on their HTTP\n86: //   headers (or other dynamic metadata) and more carefully examine others.\n87: // * A server may asynchronously monitor traffic coming through the filter by inspecting\n88: //   headers, bodies, or both, and then decide to switch to a synchronous processing\n89: //   mode, either permanently or temporarily.\n90: //\n91: // The protocol itself is based on a bidirectional gRPC stream. Envoy will send the\n92: // server\n93: // :ref:`ProcessingRequest <envoy_v3_api_msg_service.ext_proc.v3.ProcessingRequest>`\n94: // messages, and the server must reply with\n95: // :ref:`ProcessingResponse <envoy_v3_api_msg_service.ext_proc.v3.ProcessingResponse>`.\n96: //\n97: // Stats about each gRPC call are recorded in a :ref:`dynamic filter state\n98: // <arch_overview_advanced_filter_state_sharing>` object in a namespace matching the filter\n99: // name.\n100: //\n101: // [#next-free-field: 20]\n102: message ExternalProcessor {\n103:   // Describes the route cache action to be taken when an external processor response\n104:   // is received in response to request headers.\n105:   enum RouteCacheAction {\n106:     // The default behavior is to clear the route cache only when the\n107:     // :ref:`clear_route_cache <envoy_v3_api_field_service.ext_proc.v3.CommonResponse.clear_route_cache>`\n108:     // field is set in an external processor response.\n109:     DEFAULT = 0;\n110: \n111:     // Always clear the route cache irrespective of the clear_route_cache bit in\n112:     // the external processor response.\n113:     CLEAR = 1;\n114: \n115:     // Do not clear the route cache irrespective of the clear_route_cache bit in\n116:     // the external processor response. By default, request and response headers are sent,\\n27:     // while trailers are skipped.\\n28:     DEFAULT = 0;\\n29: \\n30:     // Send the header or trailer.\\n31:     SEND = 1;\\n32: \\n33:     // Do not send the header or trailer.\\n34:     SKIP = 2;\\n35:   }\\n36: \\n37:   // Control how the request and response bodies are handled\\n38:   // When body mutation by external processor is enabled, ext_proc filter will always remove\\n39:   // the content length header in three cases below because content length can not be guaranteed\\n40:   // to be set correctly:\\n41:   // 1) STREAMED BodySendMode: header processing completes before body mutation comes back.\\n42:   // 2) BUFFERED_PARTIAL BodySendMode: body is buffered and could be injected in different phases.\\n43:   // 3) BUFFERED BodySendMode + SKIP HeaderSendMode: header processing (e.g., update content-length) is skipped.\\n44:   //\\n45:   // In Envoy's http1 codec implementation, removing content length will enable chunked transfer\\n46:   // encoding whenever feasible. The recipient (either client or server) must be able\\n47:   // to parse and decode the chunked transfer coding.\\n48:   // (see `details in RFC9112 <https://tools.ietf.org/html/rfc9112#section-7.1>`_).\\n49:   //\\n50:   // In BUFFERED BodySendMode + SEND HeaderSendMode, content length header is allowed but it is\\n51:   // external processor's responsibility to set the content length correctly matched to the length\\n52:   // of mutated body. The processing service itself implements a gRPC interface that allows\\n10: it to respond to events in the lifecycle of an HTTP request / response by examining\\n11: and modifying the headers, body, and trailers of each message, or by returning a brand-new response.\\n12: \\n13: The protocol itself is based on a bidirectional gRPC stream. Envoy will send the\\n14: external processor\\n15: :ref:`ProcessingRequest <envoy_v3_api_msg_service.ext_proc.v3.ProcessingRequest>`\\n16: messages, and the processor must reply with\\n17: :ref:`ProcessingResponse <envoy_v3_api_msg_service.ext_proc.v3.ProcessingResponse>`\\n18: messages.\\n19: \\n20: Configuration options are provided to control which events are sent to the processor.\\n21: This way, the processor may receive headers, body, and trailers for both\\n22: request and response in any combination. The processor may also change this configuration\\n23: on a message-by-message basis. This allows for the construction of sophisticated processors\\n24: that decide how to respond to each message individually to eliminate unnecessary\\n25: stream requests from the proxy.\\n26: \\n27: This filter is a work in progress.   "structuredContent": {
    "content": "1: .. _config_http_filters_ext_proc:\n2: \n3: External Processing\n4: ===================\n5: * This filter should be configured with the type URL ``type.googleapis.com/envoy.extensions.filters.http.ext_proc.v3.ExternalProcessor``.\n6: * :ref:`v3 API reference <envoy_v3_api_msg_extensions.filters.http.ext_proc.v3.ExternalProcessor>`\n7: \n8: The external processing filter connects an external service, called an \"external processor,\"\n9: to the filter chain. The processing service itself implements a gRPC interface that allows\n10: it to respond to events in the lifecycle of an HTTP request / response by examining\n11: and modifying the headers, body, and trailers of each message, or by returning a brand-new response.\n12: \n13: The protocol itself is based on a bidirectional gRPC stream. Envoy will send the\n14: external processor\n15: :ref:`ProcessingRequest <envoy_v3_api_msg_service.ext_proc.v3.ProcessingRequest>`\n16: messages, and the processor must reply with\n17: :ref:`ProcessingResponse <envoy_v3_api_msg_service.ext_proc.v3.ProcessingResponse>`\n18: messages.\n19: \n20: Configuration options are provided to control which events are sent to the processor.\n21: This way, the processor may receive headers, body, and trailers for both\n22: request and response in any combination. The processor may also change this configuration\n23: on a message-by-message basis. This allows for the construction of sophisticated processors\n24: that decide how to respond to each message individually to eliminate unnecessary\n25: stream requests from the proxy.\n26: \n27: This filter is a work in progress. Most of the major bits of functionality\n28: are complete. The updated list of supported features and implementation status may\n29: be found on the :ref:`reference page <envoy_v3_api_msg_extensions.filters.http.ext_proc.v3.ExternalProcessor>`.\n30: \n31: Statistics\n32: ----------\n33: This filter outputs statistics in the\n34: ``http.<stat_prefix>.ext_proc.`` namespace. The :ref:`stat prefix\n35: <envoy_v3_api_field_extensions.filters.network.http_connection_manager.v3.HttpConnectionManager.stat_prefix>`\n36: comes from the owning HTTP connection manager.\n37: \n38: The following statistics are supported:\n39: \n40: .. csv-table::\n41:   :header: Name, Type, Description\n42:   :widths: auto\n43: \n44:   streams_started, Counter, The number of gRPC streams that have been started to send to the external processing service\n45:   streams_msgs_sent, Counter, The number of messages sent on those streams\n46:   streams_msgs_received, Counter, The number of messages received on those streams\n47:   spurious_msgs_received, Counter, The number of unexpected messages received that violated the protocol\n48:   streams_closed, Counter, The number of streams successfully closed on either end\n49:   streams_failed, Counter, The number of times a stream produced a gRPC error\n50:   failure_mode_allowed, Counter, The number of times an error was ignored due to configuration\n51:   message_timeouts, Counter, The number of times a message failed to receive a response within the configured timeout\n52:   rejected_header_mutations, Counter, The number of rejected header mutations\n53:   clear_route_cache_ignored, Counter, The number of clear cache request that were ignored\n54:   clear_route_cache_disabled, Counter, The number of clear cache requests that were rejected from being disabled\n55: ",

With this change the destructor can be called on any thread.\\n7:     This behavior can be reverted by setting the runtime flag ``envoy.reloadable_features.allow_slot_destroy_on_worker_threads``\\n8:     to ``false``.\\n9: - area: ext_proc\\n10:   change: |\\n11:     Adding support for\\n12:     :ref:`route_cache_action <envoy_v3_api_field_extensions.filters.http.ext_proc.v3.ExternalProcessor.route_cache_action>`.\\n13:     It specifies the route action to be taken when an external processor response is received in response to request headers.\\n14: - area: http2\\n15:   change: |\\n16:     Changes the default value of ``envoy.reloadable_features.http2_use_oghttp2`` to ``true``. This changes the codec used for HTTP/2\\n17:     requests and responses. This behavior can be reverted by setting the feature to ``false``.\\n18: - area: http3\\n19:   change: |\\n20:     Added a happy eyeballs feature to HTTP/3 upstream, where it assuming happy eyeballs sorting results in alternating address\\n21:     families will attempt the first v4 and v6 address before giving up on HTTP/3.  This change can be reverted by setting\\n22:     ``envoy.reloadable_features.http3_happy_eyeballs`` to ``false``.\\n23: - area: http2\\n24:   change: |\\n25:     Passes HTTP/2 ``DATA`` frames through a different codec API. This behavior can be temporarily disabled by setting the runtime\\n26:     feature ``envoy.reloadable_features.http2_use_visitor_for_data`` to ``false``.\\n27: - area: runtime\\n28:   change: |\\n29:     Rejecting invalid YAML. This has been an ``ENVOY_BUG`` linked to https://github.com/envoyproxy/envoy/issues/27434\\n30:     for over a year with no hard-blockers so should be Ok. This behavior can be temporarily disabled by setting\\n31:     the runtime feature ``envoy.reloadable_features.reject_invalid_yaml`` to ``false`` but the runtime guard must be\\n32:     parsed before any invalid YAML.\\n33: - area: proxy_protocol\\n34:   change: |\\n35:     Populate typed metadata by default in proxy protocol listener. Typed metadata can be consumed as\\n36:     :ref:`TlvsMetadata type <envoy_v3_api_msg_data.core.v3.TlvsMetadata>`.\\n37:     This change can be temporarily disabled by setting the runtime flag\\n38:     ``envoy.reloadable_features.use_typed_metadata_in_proxy_protocol_listener`` to ``false``.\\n39: - area: composite_filter\\n40:   change: |\\n41:     Adding support for\\n42:     :ref:`sample_percent <envoy_v3_api_field_extensions.filters.http.composite.v3.ExecuteFilterAction.sample_percent>`.\\n43:     It specifies the probability of the action execution. If not specified, it is 100%.\\n44: - area: golang\\n45:   change: |\\n46:     Move ``Continue``, ``SendLocalReply`` and ``RecoverPanic`` from ``FilterCallbackHandler`` to ``DecoderFilterCallbacks`` and\\n47:     ``EncoderFilterCallbacks``, to support full-duplex processing.\\n48: - area: tracing/datadog\\n49:   change: |\\n50:     Disabled remote configuration by default.\\n51:     To enable this feature, use the :ref:`remote_config <envoy_v3_api_field_config.trace.v3.DatadogConfig.remote_config>` field.\\n52: - area: local_ratelimit\\n53:   change: |\\n54:     Updated the token bucket implementation to use non-timer based token bucket. The tokens will be refilled when\\n55:     the token bucket is accessed and no dependency on the timer.\\n56:     This behavior can be temporarily reverted by setting the runtime guard\\n57:     ``envoy.reloadable_features.no_timer_based_rate_limit_token_bucket`` to ``false``.\\n58: \\n59: minor_behavior_changes:\\n60: - area: ext_proc\\n61:   change: |\\n62:     Timeout errors in external processor now returns ``504 Gateway Timeout`` to downstream clients.\\n63:     The previous behavior was returning ``500 Internal Server Error``.\\n64: - area: dfp\\n65:   change: |\\n66:     Changed dynamic forward proxy so local reply errors include DNS resolution details. This behavior can be temporarily\\n67:     disabled by setting the runtime feature ``envoy.reloadable_features.dns_details`` to ``false``.\\n68: - area: grpc\\n69:   change: |\\n70:     Changes in ``AsyncStreamImpl`` and ``GoogleAsyncStreamImpl`` now propagate tracing context headers in bidirectional streams when using\\n71:     :ref:`Envoy gRPC client <envoy_v3_api_field_config.core.v3.GrpcService.envoy_grpc>` or\\n72:     :ref:`Google C++ gRPC client <envoy_v3_api_field_config.core.v3.GrpcService.google_grpc>`. Previously, tracing context headers\\n73:     were not being set when calling external services such as ext_proc.\\n74: - area: http\\n75:   change: |\\n76:     Fixed host header changes for shadow requests to properly handle ipv6 addresses.\\n77: - area: tracers\\n78:   change: |\\n79:     Set status code for OpenTelemetry tracers (previously unset).\\n80: - area: config\\n81:   change: |\\n82:     Stricter validation of a ``google.protobuf.Duration`` field in a config, rejecting invalid values (where the number\\n83:     of years is over 292). This can be temporarily reverted by setting runtime guard\\n84:     ``envoy.reloadable_features.strict_duration_validation`` to ``false``.\\n85: - area: xds\\n86:   change: |\\n87:     Updated xDS-TP path naming to better comply with RFC-3986. Encoded resource paths can now include an a colon ``:``,\\n88:     instead of ``%3A``. This behavior can be reverted by setting the runtime flag\\n89:     ``envoy.reloadable_features.xdstp_path_avoid_colon_encoding`` to ``false``.\\n90: - area: udp\\n91:   change: |\\n92:     Change GRO read buffer to 64kB to avoid ``MSG_TRUNC``. And change the way to limit the number of packets processed per event\\n93:     loop to work with GRO. This behavior can be reverted by setting runtime guard\\n94:     ``envoy.reloadable_features.udp_socket_apply_aggregated_read_limit`` to ``false``.\\n95: - area: statistics\\n96:   change: |\\n97:     Hot restart statistics like ``hot_restart_epoch`` are only set when hot restart is enabled.\\n98: - area: dns\\n99:   change: |\\n100:     Changes the behavior of the ``getaddrinfo`` DNS resolver so that it treats ``EAI_NODATA`` and ``EAI_NONAME``\\n101:     as successful queries with empty results, instead of as DNS failures. This change brings the\\n102:     ``getaddrinfo`` behavior in-line with the c-ares resolver behavior. This behavior can be reverted by\\n103:     setting the runtime guard ``envoy.reloadable_features.dns_nodata_noname_is_success`` to ``false``.\\n104: - area: access_log\\n105:   change: |\\n106:     The upstream connection address, rather than the upstream host address, will be used for the ``%UPSTREAM_REMOTE_ADDRESS%``,\\n107:     ``%UPSTREAM_REMOTE_PORT%`` and ``%UPSTREAM_REMOTE_ADDRESS_WITHOUT_PORT%`` access log format specifiers.\\n108:     This behavior can be reverted by setting the runtime guard\\n109:     ``envoy.reloadable_features.upstream_remote_address_use_connection`` to ``false``.\\n110: - area: access_log\\n111:   change: |\\n112:     The ``%CEL%`` formatter supports call functions.\\n113: - area: http\\n114:   change: |\\n115:     Changing header validation checks in the substitution format utility and CEL code to do RFC-compliant header validation.\\n116:     This behavior can be reverted by setting the runtime guard ``envoy.reloadable_features.consistent_header_validation`` to ``false``.\\n117: - area: quic\\n118:   change: |\\n119:     Cache source/destination address instances in a LRU cache for packet read to improve performance.\\n120:     This behavior can be reverted by setting the runtime guard\\n121:     ``envoy.reloadable_features.quic_upstream_socket_use_address_cache_for_read`` to ``false``.\\n122: - area: quic\\n123:   change: |\\n124:     When a quic connection socket is created, the socket's detected transport protocol will be set to ``quic``.\\n125: - area: config\\n126:   change: |\\n127:     In xDS configuration, the :ref:`AUTO <envoy_v3_api_enum_value_config.core.v3.ApiVersion.AUTO>` value now means\\n128:     :ref:`V3 <envoy_v3_api_enum_value_config.core.v3.ApiVersion.V3>`. :ref:`AUTO <envoy_v3_api_enum_value_config.core.v3.ApiVersion.AUTO>`\\n129:     is the default value of the enum, so this field may be omitted from all configurations now.\\n130: - area: filters\\n131:   change: |\\n132:     Set ``WWW-Authenticate`` header for ``401`` responses from the Basic Auth filter.\\n133: - area: jwt_authn\\n134:   change: |\\n135:     jwt_authn now validates provider URIs. If the validation is too strict it can temporarily be\\n136:     disabled by setting the runtime guard ``envoy.reloadable_features.jwt_authn_validate_uri`` to\\n137:     ``false``.\\n138: - area: http\\n139:   change: |\\n140:     Removed runtime guard ``envoy.reloadable_features.refresh_rtt_after_request`` and legacy code path.\\n141: - area: http\\n142:   change: |\\n143:     Changing HTTP/2 semi-colon prefixed headers to being sanitized by Envoy code rather than nghttp2. Should be a functional no-op but\\n144:     guarded by ``envoy.reloadable_features.sanitize_http2_headers_without_nghttp2``.\\n145: - area: http\\n146:   change: |\\n147:     Envoy will now proxy ``104`` headers from upstream, though as with ``100`` only the first 1xx response\\n148:     headers will be sent. ``104`` headers are designated by IETF's draft-ietf-httpbis-resumable-upload RFC.\\n149:     This behavioral can be temporarily reverted by setting runtime guard\\n150:     ``envoy.reloadable_features.proxy_104`` to ``false``.\\n151: - area: jwt_authn\\n152:   change: |\\n153:     Changes the behavior of the\\n154:     :ref:`forward <envoy_v3_api_field_extensions.filters.http.jwt_authn.v3.JwtProvider.forward>`\\n155:     config. Previously, the config only removes JWT if set in headers. With this addition, the config can also be\\n156:     used to remove JWT set in query parameters. This behavior can be reverted by setting the runtime guard\\n157:     ``envoy.reloadable_features.jwt_authn_remove_jwt_from_query_params`` to ``false``.\\n158: - area: custom response filter\\n159:   change: |\\n160:     Prevent the redirect policy from sending ``100`` as the overridden response code as the custom response must\\n161:     be complete.\\n162: - area: http\\n163:   change: |\\n164:     Reject messages with chunked transfer encoding with chunk extension containing ``CR`` not followed by ``LF``. This can be\\n165:     temporarily reverted by setting runtime guard ``envoy.reloadable_features.http1_balsa_disallow_lone_cr_in_chunk_extension``\\n166:     to ``false``.\\n167: - area: quic\\n168:   change: |\\n169:     A change in QUICHE has renamed all flags formerly of the form ``quic_reloadable_flag_...`` to ``quiche_reloadable_flag_...``.\\n170:     Likewise, for ``quic_restart_flag_...``, now ``quiche_restart_flag_...``. Consequently, all Envoy flags of those forms with an\\n171:     ``envoy_quic_...`` prefix have been similarly renamed to ``envoy_quiche_...``.\\n172: - area: hashing\\n173:   change: |\\n174:     Change murmurHash2 hashing on big endian platforms to generate the same values as little endian platforms.\\n175: - area: gcp_authn\\n176:   change: |\\n177:     Use the fixed URL format instead of one from the configuration. This behavior can be disabled by setting runtime flag\\n178:     ``envoy.reloadable_features.gcp_authn_use_fixed_url`` to false.\\n179: \\n180: bug_fixes:\\n181: - area: admission control\\n182:   change: |\\n183:     Fixed the thread-local controller's average RPS calculation to be calculated over the full\\n184:     lookback window. Previously, the controller would calculate the average RPS over the amount of\\n185:     time elapsed since the oldest valid request sample. This change brings the behavior in line with\\n186:     the documentation.\\n187: - area: outlier detection\\n188:   change: |\\n189:     Fixed :ref:`successful_active_health_check_uneject_host\\n190:     <envoy_v3_api_field_config.cluster.v3.OutlierDetection.successful_active_health_check_uneject_host>`.\\n191:     Before, a failed health check could uneject the host if the ``FAILED_ACTIVE_HC`` health flag had not been set.\\n192: - area: quic\\n193:   change: |\\n194:     Applied 2 QUICHE patches for crash bugs in ``QuicSpdyStream`` ``OnDataAvailable()`` and ``OnInitialHeaderComplete()``.\\n195: - area: quic\\n196:   change: |\\n197:     Fixed crash bug when QUIC downstream stream was read closed and then timed out.\\n198: - area: tls\\n199:   change: |\\n200:     Fix a ``RELEASE_ASSERT`` when using :ref:`auto_sni <envoy_v3_api_field_config.core.v3.UpstreamHttpProtocolOptions.auto_sni>`\\n201:     if the downstream request ``:authority`` was longer than 255 characters.\\n202: - area: tracing\\n203:   change: |\\n204:     Fix an issue where span id is missing from OpenTelemetry access log entries.\\n205: - area: ext_authz\\n206:   change: |\\n207:     Added field\\n208:     :ref:`validate_mutations <envoy_v3_api_field_extensions.filters.http.ext_authz.v3.ExtAuthz.validate_mutations>`,\\n209:     which, when set to ``true``, adds header and query parameter mutation validation to the HTTP ext_authz\\n210:     filter. If you use ext_authz with an untrusted side stream,\\n212:     it's recommended you set this to ``true``.\\n213: - area: http\\n214:   change: |\\n215:     Fix a crash when reloading the HTTP Connection Manager via ECDS.\\n216: - area: cares\\n217:   change: |\\n218:     Upgraded c-ares library to 1.20.1 and added fix to c-ares DNS implementation to additionally check for ``ARES_EREFUSED``,\\n219:     ``ARES_ESERVFAIL`` and ``ARES_ENOTIMP`` status. These are only populated if a non-shadow engine exists.\\n490: - area: jwt_authn\\n491:   change: |\\n492:     Added :ref:`strip_failure_response\\n493:     <envoy_v3_api_field_extensions.filters.http.jwt_authn.v3.JwtAuthentication.strip_failure_response>`\\n494:     to allow stripping the failure response details from the JWT authentication filter.\\n495: - area: formatter\\n496:   change: |\\n497:     Added formatters for :ref:`METADATA(VIRTUAL_HOST)<envoy_v3_api_msg_extensions.formatter.metadata.v3.Metadata>`.\\n498: - area: quic\\n499:   change: |\\n500:     Added new interface to ``QuicListenerFilter`` that is called on receiving the first packet.\\n501: - area: quic\\n502:   change: |\\n503:     Added :ref:`DataSourceServerPreferredAddressConfig\\n504:     <envoy_v3_api_msg_extensions.quic.server_preferred_address.v3.DataSourceServerPreferredAddressConfig>` for cases when\\n505:     the control plane does not know the correct configuration for the server preferred address.\\n506: - area: tls\\n507:   change: |\\n508:     Added support to match against ``OtherName`` SAN-type under :ref:`match_typed_subject_alt_names\\n509:     <envoy_v3_api_field_extensions.transport_sockets.tls.v3.CertificateValidationContext.match_typed_subject_alt_names>`.\\n510:     An additional field ``oid`` is added to :ref:`SubjectAltNameMatcher\\n511:     <envoy_v3_api_msg_extensions.transport_sockets.tls.v3.SubjectAltNameMatcher>` to support this change.\\n512: - area: retry\\n513:   change: |\\n514:     Added :ref:`reset-before-request retry policy <config_http_filters_router_x-envoy-retry-on>`.\\n515: - area: ext_proc\\n516:   change: |\\n517:     Added support for observability mode which deprecates ``async_mode``. If enabled, each part of the HTTP request or response\\n518:     specified by ``ProcessingMode`` is sent without waiting for the response from the ext_proc service. It is \\\"Send and Go\\\" mode\\n519:     that can be used by external processor to observe Envoy data and status.\\n520: - area: grpc\\n521:   change: |\\n522:     Added support for flow control in Envoy gRPC side stream. This behavior can be disabled by setting the runtime flag\\n523:     ``envoy.reloadable_features.grpc_side_stream_flow_control`` to ``false``.\\n524: - area: oauth\\n525:   change: |\\n526:     Added :ref:`disable_id_token_set_cookie <envoy_v3_api_field_extensions.filters.http.oauth2.v3.OAuth2Config.disable_id_token_set_cookie>`\\n527:     to disable setting the ID Token cookie.\\n528: - area: dns_filter\\n529:   change: |\\n530:     Added support for wildcard resolution in :ref:`inline_dns_table\\n531:     <envoy_v3_api_field_extensions.filters.udp.dns_filter.v3.DnsFilterConfig.ServerContextConfig.inline_dns_table>`\\n532:     when DNS filter is working in server mode.\\n533: - area: quic\\n534:   change: |\\n535:     QUIC stream reset error code will be added to transport failure reason.\\n536:     This behavior can be reverted by setting the runtime flag ``envoy.reloadable_features.report_stream_reset_error_code``\\n537:     to ``false``.\\n538: \\n539: deprecated:\\n540: - area: tracing\\n541:   change: |\\n542:     Disable OpenCensus by default, as it is\\n543:     `no longer supported/maintained upstream <https://opentelemetry.io/blog/2023/sunsetting-opencensus/>`_.\\n544:     This extension can be replaced with the OpenTelemetry tracer and collector.\\n545: \",\"url\":\"https://sourcegraph.sourcegraph.com/github.com/sg-benchmarks/envoy--7b8baff1@7d6a8ad71741583b3a75f94937b6f294b39e2667/-/blob/changelogs/current.yaml\"}",

    "content": "1: date: July 19, 2024\n2: \n3: behavior_changes:\n4: - area: thread_local\n5:   change: |\n6:     Changes the behavior of the ``SlotImpl`` class destructor. With this change the destructor can be called on any thread.\n7:     This behavior can be reverted by setting the runtime flag ``envoy.reloadable_features.allow_slot_destroy_on_worker_threads``\n8:     to ``false``.\n9: - area: ext_proc\n10:   change: |\n11:     Adding support for\n12:     :ref:`route_cache_action <envoy_v3_api_field_extensions.filters.http.ext_proc.v3.ExternalProcessor.route_cache_action>`.\n13:     It specifies the route action to be taken when an external processor response is received in response to request headers.\n14: - area: http2\n15:   change: |\n16:     Changes the default value of ``envoy.reloadable_features.http2_use_oghttp2`` to ``true``. This changes the codec used for HTTP/2\n17:     requests and responses. This behavior can be reverted by setting the feature to ``false``.\n18: - area: http3\n19:   change: |\n20:     Added a happy eyeballs feature to HTTP/3 upstream, where it assuming happy eyeballs sorting results in alternating address\n21:     families will attempt the first v4 and v6 address before giving up on HTTP/3.  This change can be reverted by setting\n22:     ``envoy.reloadable_features.http3_happy_eyeballs`` to ``false``.\n23: - area: http2\n24:   change: |\n25:     Passes HTTP/2 ``DATA`` frames through a different codec API. This behavior can be temporarily disabled by setting the runtime\n26:     feature ``envoy.reloadable_features.http2_use_visitor_for_data`` to ``false``.\n27: - area: runtime\n28:   change: |\n29:     Rejecting invalid YAML. This has been an ``ENVOY_BUG`` linked to https://github.com/envoyproxy/envoy/issues/27434\n30:     for over a year with no hard-blockers so should be Ok. This behavior can be temporarily disabled by setting\n31:     the runtime feature ``envoy.reloadable_features.reject_invalid_yaml`` to ``false`` but the runtime guard must be\n32:     parsed before any invalid YAML.\n33: - area: proxy_protocol\n34:   change: |\n35:     Populate typed metadata by default in proxy protocol listener. Typed metadata can be consumed as\n36:     :ref:`TlvsMetadata type <envoy_v3_api_msg_data.core.v3.TlvsMetadata>`.\n37:     This change can be temporarily disabled by setting the runtime flag\n38:     ``envoy.reloadable_features.use_typed_metadata_in_proxy_protocol_listener`` to ``false``.\n39: - area: composite_filter\n40:   change: |\n41:     Adding support for\n42:     :ref:`sample_percent <envoy_v3_api_field_extensions.filters.http.composite.v3.ExecuteFilterAction.sample_percent>`.\n43:     It specifies the probability of the action execution. If not specified, it is 100%.\n44: - area: golang\n45:   change: |\n46:     Move ``Continue``, ``SendLocalReply`` and ``RecoverPanic`` from ``FilterCallbackHandler`` to ``DecoderFilterCallbacks`` and\n47:     ``EncoderFilterCallbacks``, to support full-duplex processing.\n48: - area: tracing/datadog\n49:   change: |\n50:     Disabled remote configuration by default.\n51:     To enable this feature, use the :ref:`remote_config <envoy_v3_api_field_config.trace.v3.DatadogConfig.remote_config>` field.\n52: - area: local_ratelimit\n53:   change: |\n54:     Updated the token bucket implementation to use non-timer based token bucket. The tokens will be refilled when\n55:     the token bucket is accessed and no dependency on the timer.\n56:     This behavior can be temporarily reverted by setting the runtime guard\n57:     ``envoy.reloadable_features.no_timer_based_rate_limit_token_bucket`` to ``false``.\n58: \n59: minor_behavior_changes:\n60: - area: ext_proc\n61:   change: |\n62:     Timeout errors in external processor now returns ``504 Gateway Timeout`` to downstream clients.\n63:     The previous behavior was returning ``500 Internal Server Error``.\n64: - area: dfp\n65:   change: |\n66:     Changed dynamic forward proxy so local reply errors include DNS resolution details. This behavior can be temporarily\n67:     disabled by setting the runtime feature ``envoy.reloadable_features.dns_details`` to ``false``.\n68: - area: grpc\n69:   change: |\n70:     Changes in ``AsyncStreamImpl`` and ``GoogleAsyncStreamImpl`` now propagate tracing context headers in bidirectional streams when using\n71:     :ref:`Envoy gRPC client <envoy_v3_api_field_config.core.v3.GrpcService.envoy_grpc>` or\n72:     :ref:`Google C++ gRPC client <envoy_v3_api_field_config.core.v3.GrpcService.google_grpc>`. Previously, tracing context headers\n73:     were not being set when calling external services such as ext_proc.\n74: - area: http\n75:   change: |\n76:     Fixed host header changes for shadow requests to properly handle ipv6 addresses.\n77: - area: tracers\n78:   change: |\n79:     Set status code for OpenTelemetry tracers (previously unset).\n80: - area: config\n81:   change: |\n82:     Stricter validation of a ``google.protobuf.Duration`` field in a config, rejecting invalid values (where the number\n83:     of years is over 292). This can be temporarily reverted by setting runtime guard\n84:     ``envoy.reloadable_features.strict_duration_validation`` to ``false``.\n85: - area: xds\n86:   change: |\n87:     Updated xDS-TP path naming to better comply with RFC-3986. Encoded resource paths can now include an a colon ``:``,\n88:     instead of ``%3A``. This behavior can be reverted by setting the runtime flag\n89:     ``envoy.reloadable_features.xdstp_path_avoid_colon_encoding`` to ``false``.\n90: - area: udp\n91:   change: |\n92:     Change GRO read buffer to 64kB to avoid ``MSG_TRUNC``. And change the way to limit the number of packets processed per event\n93:     loop to work with GRO. This behavior can be reverted by setting runtime guard\n94:     ``envoy.reloadable_features.udp_socket_apply_aggregated_read_limit`` to ``false``.\n95: - area: statistics\n96:   change: |\n97:     Hot restart statistics like ``hot_restart_epoch`` are only set when hot restart is enabled.\n98: - area: dns\n99:   change: |\n100:     Changes the behavior of the ``getaddrinfo`` DNS resolver so that it treats ``EAI_NODATA`` and ``EAI_NONAME``\n101:     as successful queries with empty results, instead of as DNS failures. This change brings the\n102:     ``getaddrinfo`` behavior in-line with the c-ares resolver behavior. This behavior can be reverted by\n103:     setting the runtime guard ``envoy.reloadable_features.dns_nodata_noname_is_success`` to ``false``.\n104: - area: access_log\n105:   change: |\n106:     The upstream connection address, rather than the upstream host address, will be used for the ``%UPSTREAM_REMOTE_ADDRESS%``,\n107:     ``%UPSTREAM_REMOTE_PORT%`` and ``%UPSTREAM_REMOTE_ADDRESS_WITHOUT_PORT%`` access log format specifiers.\n108:     This behavior can be reverted by setting the runtime guard\n109:     ``envoy.reloadable_features.upstream_remote_address_use_connection`` to ``false``.\n110: - area: access_log\n111:   change: |\n112:     The ``%CEL%`` formatter supports call functions.\n113: - area: http\n114:   change: |\n115:     Changing header validation checks in the substitution format utility and CEL code to do RFC-compliant header validation.\n116:     This behavior can be reverted by setting the runtime guard ``envoy.reloadable_features.consistent_header_validation`` to ``false``.\n117: - area: quic\n118:   change: |\n119:     Cache source/destination address instances in a LRU cache for packet read to improve performance.\n120:     This behavior can be reverted by setting the runtime guard\n121:     ``envoy.reloadable_features.quic_upstream_socket_use_address_cache_for_read`` to ``false``.\n122: - area: quic\n123:   change: |\n124:     When a quic connection socket is created, the socket's detected transport protocol will be set to ``quic``.\n125: - area: config\n126:   change: |\n127:     In xDS configuration, the :ref:`AUTO <envoy_v3_api_enum_value_config.core.v3.ApiVersion.AUTO>` value now means\n128:     :ref:`V3 <envoy_v3_api_enum_value_config.core.v3.ApiVersion.V3>`. :ref:`AUTO <envoy_v3_api_enum_value_config.core.v3.ApiVersion.AUTO>`\n129:     is the default value of the enum, so this field may be omitted from all configurations now.\n130: - area: filters\n131:   change: |\n132:     Set ``WWW-Authenticate`` header for ``401`` responses from the Basic Auth filter.\n133: - area: jwt_authn\n134:   change: |\n135:     jwt_authn now validates provider URIs. If the validation is too strict it can temporarily be\n136:     disabled by setting the runtime guard ``envoy.reloadable_features.jwt_authn_validate_uri`` to\n137:     ``false``.\n138: - area: http\n139:   change: |\n140:     Removed runtime guard ``envoy.reloadable_features.refresh_rtt_after_request`` and legacy code path.\n141: - area: http\n142:   change: |\n143:     Changing HTTP/2 semi-colon prefixed headers to being sanitized by Envoy code rather than nghttp2. Should be a functional no-op but\n144:     guarded by ``envoy.reloadable_features.sanitize_http2_headers_without_nghttp2``.\n145: - area: http\n146:   change: |\n147:     Envoy will now proxy ``104`` headers from upstream, though as with ``100`` only the first 1xx response\n148:     headers will be sent. ``104`` headers are designated by IETF's draft-ietf-httpbis-resumable-upload RFC.\n149:     This behavioral can be temporarily reverted by setting runtime guard\n150:     ``envoy.reloadable_features.proxy_104`` to ``false``.\n151: - area: jwt_authn\n152:   change: |\n153:     Changes the behavior of the\n154:     :ref:`forward <envoy_v3_api_field_extensions.filters.http.jwt_authn.v3.JwtProvider.forward>`\n155:     config. Previously, the config only removes JWT if set in headers. With this addition, the config can also be\n156:     used to remove JWT set in query parameters. This behavior can be reverted by setting the runtime guard\n157:     ``envoy.reloadable_features.jwt_authn_remove_jwt_from_query_params`` to ``false``.\n158: - area: custom response filter\n159:   change: |\n160:     Prevent the redirect policy from sending ``100`` as the overridden response code as the custom response must\n161:     be complete.\n162: - area: http\n163:   change: |\n164:     Reject messages with chunked transfer encoding with chunk extension containing ``CR`` not followed by ``LF``. This can be\n165:     temporarily reverted by setting runtime guard ``envoy.reloadable_features.http1_balsa_disallow_lone_cr_in_chunk_extension``\n166:     to ``false``.\n167: - area: quic\n168:   change: |\n169:     A change in QUICHE has renamed all flags formerly of the form ``quic_reloadable_flag_...`` to ``quiche_reloadable_flag_...``.\n170:     Likewise, for ``quic_restart_flag_...``, now ``quiche_restart_flag_...``. Consequently, all Envoy flags of those forms with an\n171:     ``envoy_quic_...`` prefix have been similarly renamed to ``envoy_quiche_...``.\n172: - area: hashing\n173:   change: |\n174:     Change murmurHash2 hashing on big endian platforms to generate the same values as little endian platforms.\n175: - area: gcp_authn\n176:   change: |\n177:     Use the fixed URL format instead of one from the configuration. This behavior can be disabled by setting runtime flag\n178:     ``envoy.reloadable_features.gcp_authn_use_fixed_url`` to false.\n179: \n180: bug_fixes:\n181: - area: admission control\n182:   change: |\n183:     Fixed the thread-local controller's average RPS calculation to be calculated over the full\n184:     lookback window. Previously, the controller would calculate the average RPS over the amount of\n185:     time elapsed since the oldest valid request sample. This change brings the behavior in line with\n186:     the documentation.\n187: - area: outlier detection\n188:   change: |\n189:     Fixed :ref:`successful_active_health_check_uneject_host\n190:     <envoy_v3_api_field_config.cluster.v3.OutlierDetection.successful_active_health_check_uneject_host>`.\n191:     Before, a failed health check could uneject the host if the ``FAILED_ACTIVE_HC`` health flag had not been set.\n192: - area: quic\n193:   change: |\n194:     Applied 2 QUICHE patches for crash bugs in ``QuicSpdyStream`` ``OnDataAvailable()`` and ``OnInitialHeaderComplete()``.\n195: - area: quic\n196:   change: |\n197:     Fixed crash bug when QUIC downstream stream was read closed and then timed out.\n198: - area: tls\n199:   change: |\n200:     Fix a ``RELEASE_ASSERT`` when using :ref:`auto_sni <envoy_v3_api_field_config.core.v3.UpstreamHttpProtocolOptions.auto_sni>`\n201:     if the downstream request ``:authority`` was longer than 255 characters.\n202: - area: tracing\n203:   change: |\n204:     Fix an issue where span id is missing from OpenTelemetry access log entries.\n205: - area: ext_authz\n206:   change: |\n207:     Added field\n208:     :ref:`validate_mutations <envoy_v3_api_field_extensions.filters.http.ext_authz.v3.ExtAuthz.validate_mutations>`,\n209:     which, when set to ``true``, adds header and query parameter mutation validation to the HTTP ext_authz\n210:     filter. If an authz response contains invalid mutations, the filter responds to the downstream\n211:     request with HTTP ``500 Internal Server Error``. If you use ext_authz with an untrusted side stream,\n212:     it's recommended you set this to ``true``.\n213: - area: http\n214:   change: |\n215:     Fix a crash when reloading the HTTP Connection Manager via ECDS.\n216: - area: cares\n217:   change: |\n218:     Upgraded c-ares library to 1.20.1 and added fix to c-ares DNS implementation to additionally check for ``ARES_EREFUSED``,\n219:     ``ARES_ESERVFAIL`` and ``ARES_ENOTIMP`` status. Without this fix, ``DestroyChannelOnRefused`` and\n220:     ``CustomResolverValidAfterChannelDestruction`` unit test will break.\n221: - area: udp\n222:   change: |\n223:     Fixed a bug that would cause Envoy to crash when updates to a pre-existing cluster were made (e.g. ``HostSet`` changes).\n224: - area: ext_authz\n225:   change: |\n226:     Handle ``append_action`` from :ref:`external authorization service <envoy_v3_api_msg_service.auth.v3.CheckResponse>`\n227:     that was ignored.\n228: - area: oauth2\n229:   change: |\n230:     Fixed a bug that would cause Envoy to crash when receiving an Oauth callback while the Oauth upstream is unhealthy\n231:     (e.g. due to DNS issues).\n232: - area: http\n233:   change: |\n234:     Fix BalsaParser resetting state too early, guarded by\n235:     ``envoy.reloadable_features.http1_balsa_delay_reset`` which defaults to ``true``.\n236: - area: ext_authz\n237:   change: |\n238:     Set the SNI value from the requested server name if it isn't available on the connection/socket. If the input stream has\n247:     redundant data, the decompressor will loop forever.\n248: - area: websocket\n249:   change: |\n250:     Only ``101`` is considered a successful response for websocket handshake for HTTP/1.1, and Envoy as a proxy will proxy the response\n251:     header from upstream to downstream and then close the request if other status is received.
