{
  "content": "# Envoy External Processing Filter Migration Guide\n## Version 1.30.0 \u2192 Version 1.31.0\n\n## Overview\n\nThis migration guide covers the changes to the Envoy External Processing (ext_proc) HTTP filter between versions 1.30.0 (April 2024) and 1.31.0 (July 2024). The ext_proc filter allows external gRPC services to process HTTP requests and responses by examining and modifying headers, bodies, and trailers.\n\nThe v1.31.0 release introduces significant improvements to route cache handling and adds observability mode capabilities. While most changes are backward compatible with deprecation paths, there is one breaking change to understand.\n\n---\n\n## Breaking Changes\n\n### 1. Mutual Exclusivity: `disable_clear_route_cache` vs `route_cache_action`\n\n**Impact**: Configuration validation failure if both fields are set to non-default values.\n\n**Details**:\n- In v1.30.0, `disable_clear_route_cache` was a simple boolean flag that prevented route cache clearing\n- In v1.31.0, a new `route_cache_action` enum field has been introduced that provides more granular control\n- **Both fields cannot be set to non-default values simultaneously** - the filter will fail to initialize with an `EnvoyException`\n\n**Proto Changes** (`api/envoy/extensions/filters/http/ext_proc/v3/ext_proc.proto`):\n\n```protobuf\n// v1.30.0\nmessage ExternalProcessor {\n  // ...\n  bool disable_clear_route_cache = 11;\n  // [#next-free-field: 18]\n}\n\n// v1.31.0\nmessage ExternalProcessor {\n  enum RouteCacheAction {\n    // The default behavior is to clear the route cache only when the\n    // clear_route_cache field is set in an external processor response.\n    DEFAULT = 0;\n\n    // Always clear the route cache irrespective of the clear_route_cache bit\n    // in the external processor response.\n    CLEAR = 1;\n\n    // Do not clear the route cache irrespective of the clear_route_cache bit\n    // in the external processor response. Setting to RETAIN is equivalent to\n    // set disable_clear_route_cache to true.\n    RETAIN = 2;\n  }\n\n  // Prevents clearing the route-cache when the clear_route_cache field is\n  // set in an external processor response.\n  // Only one of disable_clear_route_cache or route_cache_action can be set.\n  // It is recommended to set route_cache_action which supersedes\n  // disable_clear_route_cache.\n  bool disable_clear_route_cache = 11\n      [(udpa.annotations.field_migrate).oneof_promotion = \"clear_route_cache_type\"];\n\n  // Specifies the action to be taken when an external processor response is\n  // received in response to request headers. It is recommended to set this\n  // field than set disable_clear_route_cache.\n  // Only one of disable_clear_route_cache or route_cache_action can be set.\n  RouteCacheAction route_cache_action = 18\n      [(udpa.annotations.field_migrate).oneof_promotion = \"clear_route_cache_type\"];\n\n  // [#next-free-field: 20]\n}\n```\n\n**Migration Path**:\n\nIf your v1.30.0 configuration uses `disable_clear_route_cache`:\n\n**Before (v1.30.0)**:\n```yaml\nfilter_configs:\n  envoy.filters.http.ext_proc:\n    grpc_service: {...}\n    disable_clear_route_cache: true\n```\n\n**After (v1.31.0)**:\n```yaml\nfilter_configs:\n  envoy.filters.http.ext_proc:\n    grpc_service: {...}\n    route_cache_action: RETAIN  # Equivalent to disable_clear_route_cache: true\n```\n\nOr to use the new CLEAR behavior:\n```yaml\nfilter_configs:\n  envoy.filters.http.ext_proc:\n    grpc_service: {...}\n    route_cache_action: CLEAR  # Always clear, regardless of ext_proc response\n```\n\n**Validation Error Scenario**:\n```yaml\n# This configuration will FAIL in v1.31.0\nfilter_configs:\n  envoy.filters.http.ext_proc:\n    grpc_service: {...}\n    disable_clear_route_cache: true    # Non-default value\n    route_cache_action: CLEAR          # Non-default value\n    # Error: disable_clear_route_cache and route_cache_action cannot\n    # be set to non-default at the same time\n```\n\n**Backward Compatibility Note**:\n- Configurations with only `disable_clear_route_cache: true` will continue to work in v1.31.0\n- The filter internally converts `disable_clear_route_cache: true` to `route_cache_action: RETAIN`\n- Configurations with `disable_clear_route_cache: false` (default) can safely use the new `route_cache_action` field\n\n---\n\n## Deprecated Features\n\n### 1. `async_mode` Field Deprecation\n\n**Status**: Deprecated in favor of `observability_mode`\n\nThe `async_mode` field in the `ExternalProcessor` message remains reserved and non-functional. It has been superseded by the new `observability_mode` field which provides a \"Send and Go\" execution model.\n\n**Previous Status (v1.30.0)**:\n```protobuf\n// [#not-implemented-hide:]\n// Not implemented. Reserved for future use.\nbool async_mode = 4 [deprecated = true];\n```\n\n**Current Status (v1.31.0)**:\n```protobuf\nreserved 4;\nreserved \"async_mode\";\n\n// New replacement field\nbool observability_mode = 17;\n```\n\n**Migration Path**:\nIf you were reserving configuration space for `async_mode`, transition to `observability_mode`:\n\n```yaml\n# Before (v1.30.0) - async_mode was reserved\nfilter_configs:\n  envoy.filters.http.ext_proc:\n    # async_mode field would have gone here if implemented\n\n# After (v1.31.0) - use observability_mode instead\nfilter_configs:\n  envoy.filters.http.ext_proc:\n    observability_mode: true\n```\n\n### 2. `disable_clear_route_cache` as Primary Configuration\n\nWhile not strictly deprecated in v1.31.0, `disable_clear_route_cache` is effectively superseded by `route_cache_action`. New configurations should use `route_cache_action` for more explicit intent. The documentation explicitly recommends using `route_cache_action`.\n\n---\n\n## New Features\n\n### 1. Route Cache Action Control (`route_cache_action`)\n\n**Field**: `route_cache_action` (field 18)\n**Type**: `ExternalProcessor.RouteCacheAction` enum\n**Default**: `DEFAULT`\n\nProvides granular control over route cache behavior when the external processor responds. Replaces the binary choice offered by `disable_clear_route_cache`.\n\n**Values**:\n\n| Value | Behavior |\n|-------|----------|\n| `DEFAULT` (0) | Clear route cache only when external processor response sets `clear_route_cache: true`. This is standard behavior. |\n| `CLEAR` (1) | **Always** clear the route cache when an external processor responds to request headers, regardless of the `clear_route_cache` field in the response. |\n| `RETAIN` (2) | **Never** clear the route cache, regardless of the `clear_route_cache` field in the response. Equivalent to `disable_clear_route_cache: true`. |\n\n**Use Cases**:\n\n- **`DEFAULT`**: Standard configuration where the external processor controls route cache clearing via response messages\n- **`CLEAR`**: When you want to ensure routes are always re-evaluated after external processing, even if the processor doesn't request it (e.g., processor modifies host/authority headers)\n- **`RETAIN`**: When you want to prevent any route cache clearing, ensuring maximum performance by avoiding route re-evaluation\n\n**Configuration Example**:\n\n```yaml\n# Always clear route cache after external processing\next_proc_filter:\n  grpc_service:\n    envoy_grpc:\n      cluster_name: ext_proc_cluster\n  route_cache_action: CLEAR\n\n# Never clear route cache\next_proc_filter:\n  grpc_service:\n    envoy_grpc:\n      cluster_name: ext_proc_cluster\n  route_cache_action: RETAIN\n```\n\n### 2. Observability Mode with Deferred Stream Closure\n\n**Fields**:\n- `observability_mode` (field 17) - boolean flag\n- `deferred_close_timeout` (field 19) - Duration\n\n**Default Timeout**: 5000 milliseconds (5 seconds)\n\nIntroduces a \"Send and Go\" operational mode where the filter sends data to the external processor without waiting for responses. Useful for observability, monitoring, and audit logging use cases.\n\n**Key Characteristics**:\n\n1. **Send Without Wait**: Each part of the HTTP request/response (headers, body, trailers) is sent to the external processor without pausing filter chain iteration\n2. **Responses Ignored**: The external processor should not send processing responses - any responses received are ignored\n3. **Message Timeout Not Applied**: The `message_timeout` configuration does not apply in observability mode\n4. **Body Mode Restrictions**: Only `STREAMED` body processing mode is supported; other body modes are ignored (BUFFERED, BUFFERED_PARTIAL converted to streaming)\n5. **Deferred Stream Closure**: gRPC streams are held open longer than the client-to-backend lifetime and eventually closed based on `deferred_close_timeout`\n\n**Proto Definition**:\n\n```protobuf\nmessage ExternalProcessor {\n  // If true, send each part of the HTTP request or response specified by\n  // ProcessingMode without pausing on filter chain iteration. It is \"Send and Go\"\n  // mode that can be used by external processor to observe Envoy data and status.\n  // In this mode:\n  // 1. Only STREAMED body processing mode is supported\n  // 2. External processor should not send back processing response\n  // 3. External processor may still close the stream to indicate no more messages needed\n  bool observability_mode = 17;\n\n  // Specifies the deferred closure timeout for gRPC stream that connects to\n  // external processor. Currently, the deferred stream closure is only used in\n  // observability_mode. Default value is 5000 milliseconds (5 seconds).\n  google.protobuf.Duration deferred_close_timeout = 19;\n}\n```\n\n**Configuration Example**:\n\n```yaml\n# Basic observability mode with default 5-second timeout\next_proc_filter:\n  grpc_service:\n    envoy_grpc:\n      cluster_name: audit_logger\n  observability_mode: true\n  processing_mode:\n    request_header_mode: SEND\n    response_header_mode: SEND\n    request_body_mode: STREAMED    # Only STREAMED supported\n    response_body_mode: STREAMED   # Only STREAMED supported\n\n# Custom deferred close timeout\next_proc_filter:\n  grpc_service:\n    envoy_grpc:\n      cluster_name: audit_logger\n  observability_mode: true\n  deferred_close_timeout: 10s  # Hold streams open for 10 seconds after completion\n  processing_mode:\n    request_header_mode: SEND\n    response_header_mode: SEND\n    request_body_mode: STREAMED\n    response_body_mode: STREAMED\n```\n\n**Flow Control Note**: \u26a0\ufe0f\nThe current implementation does not have complete flow control protections. When enabling observability mode with body streaming, ensure your external processor can keep up with the data rate. The Envoy team is actively developing flow control mechanisms (tracked in [GitHub issue #33319](https://github.com/envoyproxy/envoy/issues/33319)).\n\n---\n\n## Behavioral Changes\n\n### 1. Timeout Error HTTP Status Code\n\n**Impact**: Minor but potentially observable change in error responses\n\n**Change**: When the external processor times out (fails to respond within `message_timeout`), Envoy now returns **HTTP 504 Gateway Timeout** instead of **HTTP 500 Internal Server Error**.\n\n**Details**:\n- **v1.30.0**: Timeout errors returned `500 Internal Server Error`\n- **v1.31.0**: Timeout errors return `504 Gateway Timeout`\n- **Rationale**: HTTP 504 is semantically correct for upstream service timeouts\n- **Scope**: Applies only when external processor fails to respond within the configured timeout\n\n**Configuration Impact**: None required - this is a behavioral change only\n\n**Downstream Impact**:\n- Client applications may see different status codes for ext_proc timeouts\n- Monitoring and alerting rules that specifically check for `500` errors may miss timeout-related ext_proc failures\n- Load balancers and proxies interpreting status codes may handle `504` differently than `500`\n\n**Migration Recommendations**:\n1. Update monitoring dashboards to track both `500` and `504` from ext_proc timeouts\n2. Review client-side retry logic - both 500 and 504 are typically retryable, but timeout-specific handling may be needed\n3. Update alerting rules to specifically monitor ext_proc timeout errors\n\n### 2. Proto Import Changes\n\n**Import Addition**: `udpa/annotations/migrate.proto`\n\nThe v1.31.0 proto imports the `udpa/annotations/migrate.proto` for field migration annotations related to the `route_cache_action` feature.\n\n```protobuf\n// v1.30.0\nimport \"udpa/annotations/status.proto\";\nimport \"validate/validate.proto\";\n\n// v1.31.0\nimport \"udpa/annotations/migrate.proto\";  // NEW\nimport \"udpa/annotations/status.proto\";\nimport \"validate/validate.proto\";\n```\n\n**Impact**: Minimal - only affects code generation for language bindings and doesn't change runtime behavior.\n\n---\n\n## Migration Steps\n\n### Step 1: Audit Current Configuration\n\nReview all ext_proc filter configurations in your Envoy deployments:\n\n```bash\n# Find all ext_proc configurations\ngrep -r \"envoy.filters.http.ext_proc\" <envoy-config-directory>\ngrep -r \"disable_clear_route_cache\" <envoy-config-directory>\ngrep -r \"async_mode\" <envoy-config-directory>\n```\n\n### Step 2: Update Route Cache Settings\n\nFor each configuration using `disable_clear_route_cache`:\n\n**If using `disable_clear_route_cache: true`**:\n```yaml\n# Before\next_proc:\n  grpc_service: {...}\n  disable_clear_route_cache: true\n\n# After\next_proc:\n  grpc_service: {...}\n  route_cache_action: RETAIN\n```\n\n**If relying on default behavior (`disable_clear_route_cache` absent or `false`)**:\n```yaml\n# Both work the same in v1.31.0\n# Keep as-is or explicitly set:\next_proc:\n  grpc_service: {...}\n  route_cache_action: DEFAULT  # Explicit, recommended\n```\n\n### Step 3: Plan Observability Mode Adoption\n\nIdentify if observability mode is useful for your use cases:\n\n- \u2705 Audit logging of all requests/responses\n- \u2705 Distributed tracing integration\n- \u2705 Security event collection\n- \u2705 Request/response inspection without modifying them\n- \u274c NOT for request/response modification (use standard mode)\n- \u274c NOT for conditional processing (use standard mode with mode overrides)\n\nIf adopting:\n```yaml\next_proc:\n  grpc_service:\n    envoy_grpc:\n      cluster_name: logging_service\n  observability_mode: true\n  deferred_close_timeout: 5s  # Adjust based on your logging backend\n  processing_mode:\n    request_header_mode: SEND\n    response_header_mode: SEND\n    request_body_mode: STREAMED\n    response_body_mode: STREAMED\n```\n\n### Step 4: Validate Configuration Syntax\n\nUsing `envoy --mode validate`:\n\n```bash\nenvoy --mode validate -c /path/to/envoy.yaml\n```\n\nThis will catch any mutual exclusivity violations between `disable_clear_route_cache` and `route_cache_action`.\n\n### Step 5: Update Client Error Handling\n\nIf your client applications or monitoring specifically handle ext_proc errors:\n\n1. Update status code expectations to include `504`\n2. Review retry logic for timeout handling\n3. Update logging/metrics to capture the new status codes\n\n### Step 6: Testing Checklist\n\n- [ ] All ext_proc configurations validate without errors\n- [ ] External processor service functions correctly with the new filter version\n- [ ] Route cache behavior is as expected (test with modified headers)\n- [ ] If using observability mode: verify external processor receives all expected messages\n- [ ] Timeout behavior returns `504` instead of `500`\n- [ ] No regression in request/response processing\n- [ ] Performance metrics remain stable or improve\n\n---\n\n## Testing Recommendations\n\n### Test Route Cache Action Behavior\n\n```python\n# Test CLEAR action\ndef test_route_cache_action_clear():\n    # Configure ext_proc with route_cache_action: CLEAR\n    # Send request that causes external processor to modify host header\n    # Verify that route is re-evaluated despite processor not setting\n    # clear_route_cache in response\n    pass\n\n# Test RETAIN action\ndef test_route_cache_action_retain():\n    # Configure ext_proc with route_cache_action: RETAIN\n    # Send request that causes external processor to modify host header\n    # Verify that route is NOT re-evaluated even if processor sets\n    # clear_route_cache in response\n    pass\n\n# Test mutual exclusivity validation\ndef test_mutual_exclusivity():\n    # Attempt to configure both disable_clear_route_cache: true\n    # and route_cache_action: CLEAR\n    # Verify that filter initialization fails\n    pass\n```\n\n### Test Observability Mode\n\n```python\n# Test observability mode with body streaming\ndef test_observability_mode_streaming():\n    # Configure ext_proc with observability_mode: true\n    # Send multi-part request with body\n    # Verify that external processor receives all parts\n    # Verify that filter does not wait for responses\n    # Verify that main request processing continues without blocking\n    pass\n\n# Test deferred stream closure\ndef test_deferred_close_timeout():\n    # Configure observability_mode: true with short timeout (1-2 seconds)\n    # Send request\n    # Monitor gRPC stream\n    # Verify stream closes after deferred_close_timeout elapses\n    pass\n\n# Test body mode handling\ndef test_observability_mode_body_modes():\n    # Configure observability_mode: true with BUFFERED body mode\n    # Verify that BUFFERED is converted to STREAMED behavior\n    # Verify data is streamed correctly\n    pass\n```\n\n### Test Error Status Codes\n\n```python\ndef test_timeout_returns_504():\n    # Configure ext_proc with short message_timeout\n    # Configure external processor to never respond\n    # Send request\n    # Verify that response status code is 504, not 500\n    pass\n```\n\n---\n\n## Rollback Guidance\n\n### If Issues Occur After Upgrade\n\n#### Scenario 1: Configuration Validation Fails\n\n**Error**:\n```\nEnvoyException: disable_clear_route_cache and route_cache_action cannot\nbe set to non-default at the same time.\n```\n\n**Resolution**:\n1. Remove the `route_cache_action` field from your configuration\n2. Keep only `disable_clear_route_cache` as it was in v1.30.0\n3. The filter will continue to work with the legacy field\n\n```yaml\n# Rollback configuration\next_proc:\n  grpc_service: {...}\n  disable_clear_route_cache: true  # Works in v1.31.0\n  # Remove route_cache_action field entirely\n```\n\n#### Scenario 2: Observability Mode Issues\n\n**Problem**: External processor being overwhelmed by observability mode data\n\n**Resolution**:\n1. Disable observability mode\n2. Return to standard synchronous mode\n3. Optionally enable body streaming with careful timeout tuning\n\n```yaml\n# Rollback to standard mode\next_proc:\n  grpc_service: {...}\n  observability_mode: false  # Disable observability mode\n  processing_mode:\n    request_header_mode: SEND\n    response_header_mode: SEND\n    request_body_mode: NONE    # Don't stream bodies\n    response_body_mode: NONE\n```\n\n#### Scenario 3: Route Cache Behavior Unexpected\n\n**Problem**: Route caching behaving differently than in v1.30.0\n\n**Solution**:\n1. Explicitly set `route_cache_action: DEFAULT` to match v1.30.0 behavior\n2. Or use `route_cache_action: RETAIN` if you previously used `disable_clear_route_cache: true`\n\n```yaml\n# Explicit default behavior\next_proc:\n  grpc_service: {...}\n  route_cache_action: DEFAULT  # Matches v1.30.0 default behavior\n```\n\n#### Scenario 4: Downgrade Required\n\nIf downgrading back to v1.30.0 is necessary:\n\n1. **Remove new fields**:\n   - Remove `route_cache_action` (will cause parse errors in v1.30.0)\n   - Remove `deferred_close_timeout` (will cause parse errors in v1.30.0)\n\n2. **Restore old fields**:\n   - Use only `disable_clear_route_cache` if needed\n   - Remove `observability_mode` if set\n\n3. **Example downgrade config**:\n```yaml\n# v1.31.0 config that needs downgrade\next_proc:\n  grpc_service:\n    envoy_grpc:\n      cluster_name: ext_proc_cluster\n  route_cache_action: CLEAR        # REMOVE for v1.30.0\n  deferred_close_timeout: 5s        # REMOVE for v1.30.0\n  observability_mode: false         # REMOVE for v1.30.0\n  processing_mode:\n    request_header_mode: SEND\n    response_header_mode: SEND\n\n# v1.30.0 compatible config\next_proc:\n  grpc_service:\n    envoy_grpc:\n      cluster_name: ext_proc_cluster\n  processing_mode:\n    request_header_mode: SEND\n    response_header_mode: SEND\n```\n\n---\n\n## Summary Table\n\n| Feature | v1.30.0 | v1.31.0 | Status | Migration |\n|---------|---------|---------|--------|-----------|\n| `disable_clear_route_cache` | \u2705 Primary | \u2705 Supported | Superseded | Use `route_cache_action: RETAIN` |\n| `route_cache_action` | \u274c N/A | \u2705 Primary | New | Use for new configurations |\n| `async_mode` | \ud83d\udeab Not implemented | \ud83d\udeab Reserved | Deprecated | Use `observability_mode` |\n| `observability_mode` | \u274c N/A | \u2705 New | New | Adopt for logging/audit |\n| `deferred_close_timeout` | \u274c N/A | \u2705 New | New | Configure when using observability_mode |\n| Timeout error code | HTTP 500 | HTTP 504 | Changed | Update monitoring |\n\n---\n\n## Related Resources\n\n- Envoy External Processing Filter Documentation: https://www.envoyproxy.io/docs/envoy/latest/configuration/http/http_filters/ext_proc_filter\n- Service Proto Definition: `envoy/service/ext_proc/v3/external_processor.proto`\n- Filter Proto Definition: `api/envoy/extensions/filters/http/ext_proc/v3/ext_proc.proto`\n- GitHub Issue #33319 (Flow Control): https://github.com/envoyproxy/envoy/issues/33319\n- Envoy v1.31.0 Release Notes: https://github.com/envoyproxy/envoy/releases/tag/v1.31.0\n\n---\n\n## Questions or Issues?\n\nFor issues with the migration or to report bugs with the ext_proc filter, please refer to:\n- Envoy GitHub Issues: https://github.com/envoyproxy/envoy/issues\n- Envoy Slack Community: https://envoyproxy.slack.com\n- This guide: For clarifications or additional migration scenarios\n",

{
  "content": "# Envoy External Processing Filter Migration Guide\n## Version 1.30.0 \u2192 Version 1.31.0\n\n## Overview\n\nThis migration guide covers the changes to the Envoy External Processing (ext_proc) HTTP filter between versions 1.30.0 (April 2024) and 1.31.0 (July 2024). The ext_proc filter allows external gRPC services to process HTTP requests and responses by examining and modifying headers, bodies, and trailers.\n\nThe v1.31.0 release introduces significant improvements to route cache handling and adds observability mode capabilities. While most changes are backward compatible with deprecation paths, there is one breaking change to understand.\n\n---\n\n## Breaking Changes\n\n### 1. Mutual Exclusivity: `disable_clear_route_cache` vs `route_cache_action`\n\n**Impact**: Configuration validation failure if both fields are set to non-default values.\n\n**Details**:\n- In v1.30.0, `disable_clear_route_cache` was a simple boolean flag that prevented route cache clearing\n- In v1.31.0, a new `route_cache_action` enum field has been introduced that provides more granular control\n- **Both fields cannot be set to non-default values simultaneously** - the filter will fail to initialize with an `EnvoyException`\n\n**Proto Changes** (`api/envoy/extensions/filters/http/ext_proc/v3/ext_proc.proto`):\n\n```protobuf\n// v1.30.0\nmessage ExternalProcessor {\n  // ...\n  bool disable_clear_route_cache = 11;\n  // [#next-free-field: 18]\n}\n\n// v1.31.0\nmessage ExternalProcessor {\n  enum RouteCacheAction {\n    // The default behavior is to clear the route cache only when the\n    // clear_route_cache field is set in an external processor response.\n    DEFAULT = 0;\n\n    // Always clear the route cache irrespective of the clear_route_cache bit\n    // in the external processor response.\n    CLEAR = 1;\n\n    // Do not clear the route cache irrespective of the clear_route_cache bit\n    // in the external processor response. Setting to RETAIN is equivalent to\n    // set disable_clear_route_cache to true.\n    RETAIN = 2;\n  }\n\n  // Prevents clearing the route-cache when the clear_route_cache field is\n  // set in an external processor response.\n  // Only one of disable_clear_route_cache or route_cache_action can be set.\n  // It is recommended to set route_cache_action which supersedes\n  // disable_clear_route_cache.\n  bool disable_clear_route_cache = 11\n      [(udpa.annotations.field_migrate).oneof_promotion = \"clear_route_cache_type\"];\n\n  // Specifies the action to be taken when an external processor response is\n  // received in response to request headers. It is recommended to set this\n  // field than set disable_clear_route_cache.\n  // Only one of disable_clear_route_cache or route_cache_action can be set.\n  RouteCacheAction route_cache_action = 18\n      [(udpa.annotations.field_migrate).oneof_promotion = \"clear_route_cache_type\"];\n\n  // [#next-free-field: 20]\n}\n```\n\n**Migration Path**:\n\nIf your v1.30.0 configuration uses `disable_clear_route_cache`:\n\n**Before (v1.30.0)**:\n```yaml\nfilter_configs:\n  envoy.filters.http.ext_proc:\n    grpc_service: {...}\n    disable_clear_route_cache: true\n```\n\n**After (v1.31.0)**:\n```yaml\nfilter_configs:\n  envoy.filters.http.ext_proc:\n    grpc_service: {...}\n    route_cache_action: RETAIN  # Equivalent to disable_clear_route_cache: true\n```\n\nOr to use the new CLEAR behavior:\n```yaml\nfilter_configs:\n  envoy.filters.http.ext_proc:\n    grpc_service: {...}\n    route_cache_action: CLEAR  # Always clear, regardless of ext_proc response\n```\n\n**Validation Error Scenario**:\n```yaml\n# This configuration will FAIL in v1.31.0\nfilter_configs:\n  envoy.filters.http.ext_proc:\n    grpc_service: {...}\n    disable_clear_route_cache: true    # Non-default value\n    route_cache_action: CLEAR          # Non-default value\n    # Error: disable_clear_route_cache and route_cache_action cannot\n    # be set to non-default at the same time\n```\n\n**Backward Compatibility Note**:\n- Configurations with only `disable_clear_route_cache: true` will continue to work in v1.31.0\n- The filter internally converts `disable_clear_route_cache: true` to `route_cache_action: RETAIN`\n- Configurations with `disable_clear_route_cache: false` (default) can safely use the new `route_cache_action` field\n\n---\n\n## Deprecated Features\n\n### 1. `async_mode` Field Deprecation\n\n**Status**: Deprecated in favor of `observability_mode`\n\nThe `async_mode` field in the `ExternalProcessor` message remains reserved and non-functional. It has been superseded by the new `observability_mode` field which provides a \"Send and Go\" execution model.\n\n**Previous Status (v1.30.0)**:\n```protobuf\n// [#not-implemented-hide:]\n// Not implemented. Reserved for future use.\nbool async_mode = 4 [deprecated = true];\n```\n\n**Current Status (v1.31.0)**:\n```protobuf\nreserved 4;\nreserved \"async_mode\";\n\n// New replacement field\nbool observability_mode = 17;\n```\n\n**Migration Path**:\nIf you were reserving configuration space for `async_mode`, transition to `observability_mode`:\n\n```yaml\n# Before (v1.30.0) - async_mode was reserved\nfilter_configs:\n  envoy.filters.http.ext_proc:\n    # async_mode field would have gone here if implemented\n\n# After (v1.31.0) - use observability_mode instead\nfilter_configs:\n  envoy.filters.http.ext_proc:\n    observability_mode: true\n```\n\n### 2. `disable_clear_route_cache` as Primary Configuration\n\nWhile not strictly deprecated in v1.31.0, `disable_clear_route_cache` is effectively superseded by `route_cache_action`. New configurations should use `route_cache_action` for more explicit intent. The documentation explicitly recommends using `route_cache_action`.\n\n---\n\n## New Features\n\n### 1. Route Cache Action Control (`route_cache_action`)\n\n**Field**: `route_cache_action` (field 18)\n**Type**: `ExternalProcessor.RouteCacheAction` enum\n**Default**: `DEFAULT`\n\nProvides granular control over route cache behavior when the external processor responds. Replaces the binary choice offered by `disable_clear_route_cache`.\n\n**Values**:\n\n| Value | Behavior |\n|-------|----------|\n| `DEFAULT` (0) | Clear route cache only when external processor response sets `clear_route_cache: true`. This is standard behavior. |\n| `CLEAR` (1) | **Always** clear the route cache when an external processor responds to request headers, regardless of the `clear_route_cache` field in the response. |\n| `RETAIN` (2) | **Never** clear the route cache, regardless of the `clear_route_cache` field in the response. Equivalent to `disable_clear_route_cache: true`. |\n\n**Use Cases**:\n\n- **`DEFAULT`**: Standard configuration where the external processor controls route cache clearing via response messages\n- **`CLEAR`**: When you want to ensure routes are always re-evaluated after external processing, even if the processor doesn't request it (e.g., processor modifies host/authority headers)\n- **`RETAIN`**: When you want to prevent any route cache clearing, ensuring maximum performance by avoiding route re-evaluation\n\n**Configuration Example**:\n\n```yaml\n# Always clear route cache after external processing\next_proc_filter:\n  grpc_service:\n    envoy_grpc:\n      cluster_name: ext_proc_cluster\n  route_cache_action: CLEAR\n\n# Never clear route cache\next_proc_filter:\n  grpc_service:\n    envoy_grpc:\n      cluster_name: ext_proc_cluster\n  route_cache_action: RETAIN\n```\n\n### 2. Observability Mode with Deferred Stream Closure\n\n**Fields**:\n- `observability_mode` (field 17) - boolean flag\n- `deferred_close_timeout` (field 19) - Duration\n\n**Default Timeout**: 5000 milliseconds (5 seconds)\n\nIntroduces a \"Send and Go\" operational mode where the filter sends data to the external processor without waiting for responses. Useful for observability, monitoring, and audit logging use cases.\n\n**Key Characteristics**:\n\n1. **Send Without Wait**: Each part of the HTTP request/response (headers, body, trailers) is sent to the external processor without pausing filter chain iteration\n2. **Responses Ignored**: The external processor should not send processing responses - any responses received are ignored\n3. **Message Timeout Not Applied**: The `message_timeout` configuration does not apply in observability mode\n4. **Body Mode Restrictions**: Only `STREAMED` body processing mode is supported; other body modes are ignored (BUFFERED, BUFFERED_PARTIAL converted to streaming)\n5. **Deferred Stream Closure**: gRPC streams are held open longer than the client-to-backend lifetime and eventually closed based on `deferred_close_timeout`\n\n**Proto Definition**:\n\n```protobuf\nmessage ExternalProcessor {\n  // If true, send each part of the HTTP request or response specified by\n  // ProcessingMode without pausing on filter chain iteration. It is \"Send and Go\"\n  // mode that can be used by external processor to observe Envoy data and status.\n  // In this mode:\n  // 1. Only STREAMED body processing mode is supported\n  // 2. External processor should not send back processing response\n  // 3. External processor may still close the stream to indicate no more messages needed\n  bool observability_mode = 17;\n\n  // Specifies the deferred closure timeout for gRPC stream that connects to\n  // external processor. Currently, the deferred stream closure is only used in\n  // observability_mode. Default value is 5000 milliseconds (5 seconds).\n  google.protobuf.Duration deferred_close_timeout = 19;\n}\n```\n\n**Configuration Example**:\n\n```yaml\n# Basic observability mode with default 5-second timeout\next_proc_filter:\n  grpc_service:\n    envoy_grpc:\n      cluster_name: audit_logger\n  observability_mode: true\n  processing_mode:\n    request_header_mode: SEND\n    response_header_mode: SEND\n    request_body_mode: STREAMED    # Only STREAMED supported\n    response_body_mode: STREAMED   # Only STREAMED supported\n\n# Custom deferred close timeout\next_proc_filter:\n  grpc_service:\n    envoy_grpc:\n      cluster_name: audit_logger\n  observability_mode: true\n  deferred_close_timeout: 10s  # Hold streams open for 10 seconds after completion\n  processing_mode:\n    request_header_mode: SEND\n    response_header_mode: SEND\n    request_body_mode: STREAMED\n    response_body_mode: STREAMED\n```\n\n**Flow Control Note**: \u26a0\ufe0f\nThe current implementation does not have complete flow control protections. When enabling observability mode with body streaming, ensure your external processor can keep up with the data rate. The Envoy team is actively developing flow control mechanisms (tracked in [GitHub issue #33319](https://github.com/envoyproxy/envoy/issues/33319)).\n\n---\n\n## Behavioral Changes\n\n### 1. Timeout Error HTTP Status Code\n\n**Impact**: Minor but potentially observable change in error responses\n\n**Change**: When the external processor times out (fails to respond within `message_timeout`), Envoy now returns **HTTP 504 Gateway Timeout** instead of **HTTP 500 Internal Server Error**.\n\n**Details**:\n- **v1.30.0**: Timeout errors returned `500 Internal Server Error`\n- **v1.31.0**: Timeout errors return `504 Gateway Timeout`\n- **Rationale**: HTTP 504 is semantically correct for upstream service timeouts\n- **Scope**: Applies only when external processor fails to respond within the configured timeout\n\n**Configuration Impact**: None required - this is a behavioral change only\n\n**Downstream Impact**:\n- Client applications may see different status codes for ext_proc timeouts\n- Monitoring and alerting rules that specifically check for `500` errors may miss timeout-related ext_proc failures\n- Load balancers and proxies interpreting status codes may handle `504` differently than `500`\n\n**Migration Recommendations**:\n1. Update monitoring dashboards to track both `500` and `504` from ext_proc timeouts\n2. Review client-side retry logic - both 500 and 504 are typically retryable, but timeout-specific handling may be needed\n3. Update alerting rules to specifically monitor ext_proc timeout errors\n\n### 2. Proto Import Changes\n\n**Import Addition**: `udpa/annotations/migrate.proto`\n\nThe v1.31.0 proto imports the `udpa/annotations/migrate.proto` for field migration annotations related to the `route_cache_action` feature.\n\n```protobuf\n// v1.30.0\nimport \"udpa/annotations/status.proto\";\nimport \"validate/validate.proto\";\n\n// v1.31.0\nimport \"udpa/annotations/migrate.proto\";  // NEW\nimport \"udpa/annotations/status.proto\";\nimport \"validate/validate.proto\";\n```\n\n**Impact**: Minimal - only affects code generation for language bindings and doesn't change runtime behavior.\n\n---\n\n## Migration Steps\n\n### Step 1: Audit Current Configuration\n\nReview all ext_proc filter configurations in your Envoy deployments:\n\n```bash\n# Find all ext_proc configurations\ngrep -r \"envoy.filters.http.ext_proc\" <envoy-config-directory>\ngrep -r \"disable_clear_route_cache\" <envoy-config-directory>\ngrep -r \"async_mode\" <envoy-config-directory>\n```\n\n### Step 2: Update Route Cache Settings\n\nFor each configuration using `disable_clear_route_cache`:\n\n**If using `disable_clear_route_cache: true`**:\n```yaml\n# Before\next_proc:\n  grpc_service: {...}\n  disable_clear_route_cache: true\n\n# After\next_proc:\n  grpc_service: {...}\n  route_cache_action: RETAIN\n```\n\n**If relying on default behavior (`disable_clear_route_cache` absent or `false`)**:\n```yaml\n# Both work the same in v1.31.0\n# Keep as-is or explicitly set:\next_proc:\n  grpc_service: {...}\n  route_cache_action: DEFAULT  # Explicit, recommended\n```\n\n### Step 3: Plan Observability Mode Adoption\n\nIdentify if observability mode is useful for your use cases:\n\n- \u2705 Audit logging of all requests/responses\n- \u2705 Distributed tracing integration\n- \u2705 Security event collection\n- \u2705 Request/response inspection without modifying them\n- \u274c NOT for request/response modification (use standard mode)\n- \u274c NOT for conditional processing (use standard mode with mode overrides)\n\nIf adopting:\n```yaml\next_proc:\n  grpc_service:\n    envoy_grpc:\n      cluster_name: logging_service\n  observability_mode: true\n  deferred_close_timeout: 5s  # Adjust based on your logging backend\n  processing_mode:\n    request_header_mode: SEND\n    response_header_mode: SEND\n    request_body_mode: STREAMED\n    response_body_mode: STREAMED\n```\n\n### Step 4: Validate Configuration Syntax\n\nUsing `envoy --mode validate`:\n\n```bash\nenvoy --mode validate -c /path/to/envoy.yaml\n```\n\nThis will catch any mutual exclusivity violations between `disable_clear_route_cache` and `route_cache_action`.\n\n### Step 5: Update Client Error Handling\n\nIf your client applications or monitoring specifically handle ext_proc errors:\n\n1. Update status code expectations to include `504`\n2. Review retry logic for timeout handling\n3. Update logging/metrics to capture the new status codes\n\n### Step 6: Testing Checklist\n\n- [ ] All ext_proc configurations validate without errors\n- [ ] External processor service functions correctly with the new filter version\n- [ ] Route cache behavior is as expected (test with modified headers)\n- [ ] If using observability mode: verify external processor receives all expected messages\n- [ ] Timeout behavior returns `504` instead of `500`\n- [ ] No regression in request/response processing\n- [ ] Performance metrics remain stable or improve\n\n---\n\n## Testing Recommendations\n\n### Test Route Cache Action Behavior\n\n```python\n# Test CLEAR action\ndef test_route_cache_action_clear():\n    # Configure ext_proc with route_cache_action: CLEAR\n    # Send request that causes external processor to modify host header\n    # Verify that route is re-evaluated despite processor not setting\n    # clear_route_cache in response\n    pass\n\n# Test RETAIN action\ndef test_route_cache_action_retain():\n    # Configure ext_proc with route_cache_action: RETAIN\n    # Send request that causes external processor to modify host header\n    # Verify that route is NOT re-evaluated even if processor sets\n    # clear_route_cache in response\n    pass\n\n# Test mutual exclusivity validation\ndef test_mutual_exclusivity():\n    # Attempt to configure both disable_clear_route_cache: true\n    # and route_cache_action: CLEAR\n    # Verify that filter initialization fails\n    pass\n```\n\n### Test Observability Mode\n\n```python\n# Test observability mode with body streaming\ndef test_observability_mode_streaming():\n    # Configure ext_proc with observability_mode: true\n    # Send multi-part request with body\n    # Verify that external processor receives all parts\n    # Verify that filter does not wait for responses\n    # Verify that main request processing continues without blocking\n    pass\n\n# Test deferred stream closure\ndef test_deferred_close_timeout():\n    # Configure observability_mode: true with short timeout (1-2 seconds)\n    # Send request\n    # Monitor gRPC stream\n    # Verify stream closes after deferred_close_timeout elapses\n    pass\n\n# Test body mode handling\ndef test_observability_mode_body_modes():\n    # Configure observability_mode: true with BUFFERED body mode\n    # Verify that BUFFERED is converted to STREAMED behavior\n    # Verify data is streamed correctly\n    pass\n```\n\n### Test Error Status Codes\n\n```python\ndef test_timeout_returns_504():\n    # Configure ext_proc with short message_timeout\n    # Configure external processor to never respond\n    # Send request\n    # Verify that response status code is 504, not 500\n    pass\n```\n\n---\n\n## Rollback Guidance\n\n### If Issues Occur After Upgrade\n\n#### Scenario 1: Configuration Validation Fails\n\n**Error**:\n```\nEnvoyException: disable_clear_route_cache and route_cache_action cannot\nbe set to non-default at the same time.\n```\n\n**Resolution**:\n1. Remove the `route_cache_action` field from your configuration\n2. Keep only `disable_clear_route_cache` as it was in v1.30.0\n3. The filter will continue to work with the legacy field\n\n```yaml\n# Rollback configuration\next_proc:\n  grpc_service: {...}\n  disable_clear_route_cache: true  # Works in v1.31.0\n  # Remove route_cache_action field entirely\n```\n\n#### Scenario 2: Observability Mode Issues\n\n**Problem**: External processor being overwhelmed by observability mode data\n\n**Resolution**:\n1. Disable observability mode\n2. Return to standard synchronous mode\n3. Optionally enable body streaming with careful timeout tuning\n\n```yaml\n# Rollback to standard mode\next_proc:\n  grpc_service: {...}\n  observability_mode: false  # Disable observability mode\n  processing_mode:\n    request_header_mode: SEND\n    response_header_mode: SEND\n    request_body_mode: NONE    # Don't stream bodies\n    response_body_mode: NONE\n```\n\n#### Scenario 3: Route Cache Behavior Unexpected\n\n**Problem**: Route caching behaving differently than in v1.30.0\n\n**Solution**:\n1. Explicitly set `route_cache_action: DEFAULT` to match v1.30.0 behavior\n2. Or use `route_cache_action: RETAIN` if you previously used `disable_clear_route_cache: true`\n\n```yaml\n# Explicit default behavior\next_proc:\n  grpc_service: {...}\n  route_cache_action: DEFAULT  # Matches v1.30.0 default behavior\n```\n\n#### Scenario 4: Downgrade Required\n\nIf downgrading back to v1.30.0 is necessary:\n\n1. **Remove new fields**:\n   - Remove `route_cache_action` (will cause parse errors in v1.30.0)\n   - Remove `deferred_close_timeout` (will cause parse errors in v1.30.0)\n\n2. **Restore old fields**:\n   - Use only `disable_clear_route_cache` if needed\n   - Remove `observability_mode` if set\n\n3. **Example downgrade config**:\n```yaml\n# v1.31.0 config that needs downgrade\next_proc:\n  grpc_service:\n    envoy_grpc:\n      cluster_name: ext_proc_cluster\n  route_cache_action: CLEAR        # REMOVE for v1.30.0\n  deferred_close_timeout: 5s        # REMOVE for v1.30.0\n  observability_mode: false         # REMOVE for v1.30.0\n  processing_mode:\n    request_header_mode: SEND\n    response_header_mode: SEND\n\n# v1.30.0 compatible config\next_proc:\n  grpc_service:\n    envoy_grpc:\n      cluster_name: ext_proc_cluster\n  processing_mode:\n    request_header_mode: SEND\n    response_header_mode: SEND\n```\n\n---\n\n## Summary Table\n\n| Feature | v1.30.0 | v1.31.0 | Status | Migration |\n|---------|---------|---------|--------|-----------|\n| `disable_clear_route_cache` | \u2705 Primary | \u2705 Supported | Superseded | Use `route_cache_action: RETAIN` |\n| `route_cache_action` | \u274c N/A | \u2705 Primary | New | Use for new configurations |\n| `async_mode` | \ud83d\udeab Not implemented | \ud83d\udeab Reserved | Deprecated | Use `observability_mode` |\n| `observability_mode` | \u274c N/A | \u2705 New | New | Adopt for logging/audit |\n| `deferred_close_timeout` | \u274c N/A | \u2705 New | New | Configure when using observability_mode |\n| Timeout error code | HTTP 500 | HTTP 504 | Changed | Update monitoring |\n\n---\n\n## Related Resources\n\n- Envoy External Processing Filter Documentation: https://www.envoyproxy.io/docs/envoy/latest/configuration/http/http_filters/ext_proc_filter\n- Service Proto Definition: `envoy/service/ext_proc/v3/external_processor.proto`\n- Filter Proto Definition: `api/envoy/extensions/filters/http/ext_proc/v3/ext_proc.proto`\n- GitHub Issue #33319 (Flow Control): https://github.com/envoyproxy/envoy/issues/33319\n- Envoy v1.31.0 Release Notes: https://github.com/envoyproxy/envoy/releases/tag/v1.31.0\n\n---\n\n## Questions or Issues?\n\nFor issues with the migration or to report bugs with the ext_proc filter, please refer to:\n- Envoy GitHub Issues: https://github.com/envoyproxy/envoy/issues\n- Envoy Slack Community: https://envoyproxy.slack.com\n- This guide: For clarifications or additional migration scenarios\n",

# Envoy External Processing Filter Migration Guide
## Version 1.30.0 → Version 1.31.0

## Overview

This migration guide covers the changes to the Envoy External Processing (ext_proc) HTTP filter between versions 1.30.0 (April 2024) and 1.31.0 (July 2024). The ext_proc filter allows external gRPC services to process HTTP requests and responses by examining and modifying headers, bodies, and trailers.

The v1.31.0 release introduces significant improvements to route cache handling and adds observability mode capabilities. While most changes are backward compatible with deprecation paths, there is one breaking change to understand.

---

## Breaking Changes

### 1. Mutual Exclusivity: `disable_clear_route_cache` vs `route_cache_action`

**Impact**: Configuration validation failure if both fields are set to non-default values.

**Details**:
- In v1.30.0, `disable_clear_route_cache` was a simple boolean flag that prevented route cache clearing
- In v1.31.0, a new `route_cache_action` enum field has been introduced that provides more granular control
- **Both fields cannot be set to non-default values simultaneously** - the filter will fail to initialize with an `EnvoyException`

**Proto Changes** (`api/envoy/extensions/filters/http/ext_proc/v3/ext_proc.proto`):

```protobuf
// v1.30.0
message ExternalProcessor {
  // ...
  bool disable_clear_route_cache = 11;
  // [#next-free-field: 18]
}

// v1.31.0
message ExternalProcessor {
  enum RouteCacheAction {
    // The default behavior is to clear the route cache only when the
    // clear_route_cache field is set in an external processor response.
    DEFAULT = 0;

    // Always clear the route cache irrespective of the clear_route_cache bit
    // in the external processor response.
    CLEAR = 1;

    // Do not clear the rout
... (truncated)
